    38 â”‚ â”‚           /**
    39 â”‚ â”‚            * An enumeration describing the way in which a device
    40 â”‚ â”‚            * axis (valuator) maps onto the predefined valuator
    41 â”‚ â”‚            * types that GTK+ understands.
    42 â”‚ â”‚            *
    43 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that the X and Y axes are not really needed; pointer devices
    44 â”‚ â”‚            * report their location via the x/y members of events regardless. Whether
    45 â”‚ â”‚            * X and Y are present as axes depends on the GDK backend.
    46 â”‚ â”‚            */
    47 â”‚ â”‚   
    48 â”‚ â”‚           /**
    49 â”‚ â”‚            * An enumeration describing the way in which a device
    50 â”‚ â”‚            * axis (valuator) maps onto the predefined valuator
    51 â”‚ â”‚            * types that GTK+ understands.
    52 â”‚ â”‚            *
    53 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that the X and Y axes are not really needed; pointer devices
    54 â”‚ â”‚            * report their location via the x/y members of events regardless. Whether
    55 â”‚ â”‚            * X and Y are present as axes depends on the GDK backend.
    56 â”‚ â”‚            */
    57 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace AxisUse {
    58 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<AxisUse>;
    59 â”‚ â”‚           }
    60 â”‚ â”‚   
    61 â”‚ â”‚           enum AxisUse {
    62 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    63 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is ignored.
    64 â”‚ â”‚                */
    65 â”‚ â”‚               IGNORE,
    66 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    67 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used as the x axis.
    68 â”‚ â”‚                */
    69 â”‚ â”‚               X,
    70 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    71 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used as the y axis.
    72 â”‚ â”‚                */
    73 â”‚ â”‚               Y,
    74 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    75 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for pressure information.
    76 â”‚ â”‚                */
    77 â”‚ â”‚               PRESSURE,
    78 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    79 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for x tilt information.
    80 â”‚ â”‚                */
    81 â”‚ â”‚               XTILT,
    82 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    83 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for y tilt information.
    84 â”‚ â”‚                */
    85 â”‚ â”‚               YTILT,
    86 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    87 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for wheel information.
    88 â”‚ â”‚                */
    89 â”‚ â”‚               WHEEL,
    90 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    91 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for pen/tablet distance information. (Since: 3.22)
    92 â”‚ â”‚                */
    93 â”‚ â”‚               DISTANCE,
    94 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    95 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for pen rotation information. (Since: 3.22)
    96 â”‚ â”‚                */
    97 â”‚ â”‚               ROTATION,
    98 â”‚ â”‚               /**
    99 â”‚ â”‚                * the axis is used for pen slider information. (Since: 3.22)
   100 â”‚ â”‚                */
   101 â”‚ â”‚               SLIDER,
   102 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   103 â”‚ â”‚                * a constant equal to the numerically highest axis value.
   104 â”‚ â”‚                */
   105 â”‚ â”‚               LAST,
   106 â”‚ â”‚           }
   107 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   108 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of values describing the possible byte-orders
   109 â”‚ â”‚            * for storing pixel values in memory.
   110 â”‚ â”‚            */
   111 â”‚ â”‚   
   112 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   113 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of values describing the possible byte-orders
   114 â”‚ â”‚            * for storing pixel values in memory.
   115 â”‚ â”‚            */
   116 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace ByteOrder {
   117 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<ByteOrder>;
   118 â”‚ â”‚           }
   119 â”‚ â”‚   
   120 â”‚ â”‚           enum ByteOrder {
   121 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   122 â”‚ â”‚                * The values are stored with the least-significant byte
   123 â”‚ â”‚                *   first. For instance, the 32-bit value 0xffeecc would be stored
   124 â”‚ â”‚                *   in memory as 0xcc, 0xee, 0xff, 0x00.
   125 â”‚ â”‚                */
   126 â”‚ â”‚               LSB_FIRST,
   127 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   128 â”‚ â”‚                * The values are stored with the most-significant byte
   129 â”‚ â”‚                *   first. For instance, the 32-bit value 0xffeecc would be stored
   130 â”‚ â”‚                *   in memory as 0x00, 0xff, 0xee, 0xcc.
   131 â”‚ â”‚                */
   132 â”‚ â”‚               MSB_FIRST,
   133 â”‚ â”‚           }
   134 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   135 â”‚ â”‚            * Specifies the crossing mode for #GdkEventCrossing.
   136 â”‚ â”‚            */
   137 â”‚ â”‚   
   138 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   139 â”‚ â”‚            * Specifies the crossing mode for #GdkEventCrossing.
   140 â”‚ â”‚            */
   141 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace CrossingMode {
   142 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<CrossingMode>;
   143 â”‚ â”‚           }
   144 â”‚ â”‚   
   145 â”‚ â”‚           enum CrossingMode {
   146 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   147 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because of pointer motion.
   148 â”‚ â”‚                */
   149 â”‚ â”‚               NORMAL,
   150 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   151 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a grab is activated.
   152 â”‚ â”‚                */
   153 â”‚ â”‚               GRAB,
   154 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   155 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a grab is deactivated.
   156 â”‚ â”‚                */
   157 â”‚ â”‚               UNGRAB,
   158 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   159 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a GTK+ grab is activated.
   160 â”‚ â”‚                */
   161 â”‚ â”‚               GTK_GRAB,
   162 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   163 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a GTK+ grab is deactivated.
   164 â”‚ â”‚                */
   165 â”‚ â”‚               GTK_UNGRAB,
   166 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   167 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a GTK+ widget changed
   168 â”‚ â”‚                *   state (e.g. sensitivity).
   169 â”‚ â”‚                */
   170 â”‚ â”‚               STATE_CHANGED,
   171 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   172 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a touch sequence has begun,
   173 â”‚ â”‚                *   this event is synthetic as the pointer might have not left the window.
   174 â”‚ â”‚                */
   175 â”‚ â”‚               TOUCH_BEGIN,
   176 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   177 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because a touch sequence has ended,
   178 â”‚ â”‚                *   this event is synthetic as the pointer might have not left the window.
   179 â”‚ â”‚                */
   180 â”‚ â”‚               TOUCH_END,
   181 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   182 â”‚ â”‚                * crossing because of a device switch (i.e.
   183 â”‚ â”‚                *   a mouse taking control of the pointer after a touch device), this event
   184 â”‚ â”‚                *   is synthetic as the pointer didnâ€™t leave the window.
   185 â”‚ â”‚                */
   186 â”‚ â”‚               DEVICE_SWITCH,
   187 â”‚ â”‚           }

   671 â”‚ â”‚           enum DragProtocol {
   672 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   673 â”‚ â”‚                * no protocol.
   674 â”‚ â”‚                */
   675 â”‚ â”‚               NONE,
   676 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   677 â”‚ â”‚                * The Motif DND protocol. No longer supported
   678 â”‚ â”‚                */
   679 â”‚ â”‚               MOTIF,
   680 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   681 â”‚ â”‚                * The Xdnd protocol.
   682 â”‚ â”‚                */
   683 â”‚ â”‚               XDND,
   684 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   685 â”‚ â”‚                * An extension to the Xdnd protocol for
   686 â”‚ â”‚                *  unclaimed root window drops.
   687 â”‚ â”‚                */
   688 â”‚ â”‚               ROOTWIN,
   689 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   690 â”‚ â”‚                * The simple WM_DROPFILES protocol.
   691 â”‚ â”‚                */
   692 â”‚ â”‚               WIN32_DROPFILES,
   693 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   694 â”‚ â”‚                * The complex OLE2 DND protocol (not implemented).
   695 â”‚ â”‚                */
   696 â”‚ â”‚               OLE2,
   697 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   698 â”‚ â”‚                * Intra-application DND.
   699 â”‚ â”‚                */
   700 â”‚ â”‚               LOCAL,
   701 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   702 â”‚ â”‚                * Wayland DND protocol.
   703 â”‚ â”‚                */
   704 â”‚ â”‚               WAYLAND,
   705 â”‚ â”‚           }
   706 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   707 â”‚ â”‚            * Specifies the type of the event.
   708 â”‚ â”‚            *
   709 â”‚ â”‚            * Do not confuse these events with the signals that GTK+ widgets emit.
   710 â”‚ â”‚            * Although many of these events result in corresponding signals being emitted,
   711 â”‚ â”‚            * the events are often transformed or filtered along the way.
   712 â”‚ â”‚            *
   713 â”‚ â”‚            * In some language bindings, the values %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS and
   714 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS would translate into something syntactically
   715 â”‚ â”‚            * invalid (eg `Gdk.EventType.2ButtonPress`, where a
   716 â”‚ â”‚            * symbol is not allowed to start with a number). In that case, the
   717 â”‚ â”‚            * aliases %GDK_DOUBLE_BUTTON_PRESS and %GDK_TRIPLE_BUTTON_PRESS can
   718 â”‚ â”‚            * be used instead.
   719 â”‚ â”‚            */
   720 â”‚ â”‚   
   721 â”‚ â”‚           /**
   722 â”‚ â”‚            * Specifies the type of the event.
   723 â”‚ â”‚            *
   724 â”‚ â”‚            * Do not confuse these events with the signals that GTK+ widgets emit.
   725 â”‚ â”‚            * Although many of these events result in corresponding signals being emitted,
   726 â”‚ â”‚            * the events are often transformed or filtered along the way.
   727 â”‚ â”‚            *
   728 â”‚ â”‚            * In some language bindings, the values %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS and
   729 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS would translate into something syntactically
   730 â”‚ â”‚            * invalid (eg `Gdk.EventType.2ButtonPress`, where a
   731 â”‚ â”‚            * symbol is not allowed to start with a number). In that case, the
   732 â”‚ â”‚            * aliases %GDK_DOUBLE_BUTTON_PRESS and %GDK_TRIPLE_BUTTON_PRESS can
   733 â”‚ â”‚            * be used instead.
   734 â”‚ â”‚            */
   735 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace EventType {
   736 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<EventType>;
   737 â”‚ â”‚           }
   738 â”‚ â”‚   
   739 â”‚ â”‚           enum EventType {
   740 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   741 â”‚ â”‚                * a special code to indicate a null event.
   742 â”‚ â”‚                */
   743 â”‚ â”‚               NOTHING,
   744 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   745 â”‚ â”‚                * the window manager has requested that the toplevel window be
   746 â”‚ â”‚                *   hidden or destroyed, usually when the user clicks on a special icon in the
   747 â”‚ â”‚                *   title bar.
   748 â”‚ â”‚                */
   749 â”‚ â”‚               DELETE,
   750 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   751 â”‚ â”‚                * the window has been destroyed.
   752 â”‚ â”‚                */
   753 â”‚ â”‚               DESTROY,
   754 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   755 â”‚ â”‚                * all or part of the window has become visible and needs to be
   756 â”‚ â”‚                *   redrawn.
   757 â”‚ â”‚                */
   758 â”‚ â”‚               EXPOSE,
   759 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   760 â”‚ â”‚                * the pointer (usually a mouse) has moved.
   761 â”‚ â”‚                */
   762 â”‚ â”‚               MOTION_NOTIFY,
   763 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   764 â”‚ â”‚                * a mouse button has been pressed.
   765 â”‚ â”‚                */
   766 â”‚ â”‚               BUTTON_PRESS,
   767 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   768 â”‚ â”‚                * a mouse button has been double-clicked (clicked twice
   769 â”‚ â”‚                *   within a short period of time). Note that each click also generates a
   770 â”‚ â”‚                *   %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS event.
   771 â”‚ â”‚                */
   772 â”‚ â”‚               '2BUTTON_PRESS',
   773 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   774 â”‚ â”‚                * alias for %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS, added in 3.6.
   775 â”‚ â”‚                */
   776 â”‚ â”‚               DOUBLE_BUTTON_PRESS,
   777 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   778 â”‚ â”‚                * a mouse button has been clicked 3 times in a short period
   779 â”‚ â”‚                *   of time. Note that each click also generates a %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS event.
   780 â”‚ â”‚                */
   781 â”‚ â”‚               '3BUTTON_PRESS',
   782 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   783 â”‚ â”‚                * alias for %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS, added in 3.6.
   784 â”‚ â”‚                */
   785 â”‚ â”‚               TRIPLE_BUTTON_PRESS,
   786 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   787 â”‚ â”‚                * a mouse button has been released.
   788 â”‚ â”‚                */
   789 â”‚ â”‚               BUTTON_RELEASE,
   790 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   791 â”‚ â”‚                * a key has been pressed.
   792 â”‚ â”‚                */
   793 â”‚ â”‚               KEY_PRESS,
   794 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   795 â”‚ â”‚                * a key has been released.
   796 â”‚ â”‚                */
   797 â”‚ â”‚               KEY_RELEASE,
   798 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   799 â”‚ â”‚                * the pointer has entered the window.
   800 â”‚ â”‚                */
   801 â”‚ â”‚               ENTER_NOTIFY,
   802 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   803 â”‚ â”‚                * the pointer has left the window.
   804 â”‚ â”‚                */
   805 â”‚ â”‚               LEAVE_NOTIFY,
   806 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   807 â”‚ â”‚                * the keyboard focus has entered or left the window.
   808 â”‚ â”‚                */
   809 â”‚ â”‚               FOCUS_CHANGE,
   810 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   811 â”‚ â”‚                * the size, position or stacking order of the window has changed.
   812 â”‚ â”‚                *   Note that GTK+ discards these events for %GDK_WINDOW_CHILD windows.
   813 â”‚ â”‚                */
   814 â”‚ â”‚               CONFIGURE,
   815 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   816 â”‚ â”‚                * the window has been mapped.
   817 â”‚ â”‚                */
   818 â”‚ â”‚               MAP,
   819 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   820 â”‚ â”‚                * the window has been unmapped.
   821 â”‚ â”‚                */
   822 â”‚ â”‚               UNMAP,
   823 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   824 â”‚ â”‚                * a property on the window has been changed or deleted.
   825 â”‚ â”‚                */
   826 â”‚ â”‚               PROPERTY_NOTIFY,
   827 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   828 â”‚ â”‚                * the application has lost ownership of a selection.
   829 â”‚ â”‚                */
   830 â”‚ â”‚               SELECTION_CLEAR,
   831 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   832 â”‚ â”‚                * another application has requested a selection.
   833 â”‚ â”‚                */
   834 â”‚ â”‚               SELECTION_REQUEST,
   835 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   836 â”‚ â”‚                * a selection has been received.
   837 â”‚ â”‚                */
   838 â”‚ â”‚               SELECTION_NOTIFY,
   839 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   840 â”‚ â”‚                * an input device has moved into contact with a sensing
   841 â”‚ â”‚                *   surface (e.g. a touchscreen or graphics tablet).
   842 â”‚ â”‚                */
   843 â”‚ â”‚               PROXIMITY_IN,
   844 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   845 â”‚ â”‚                * an input device has moved out of contact with a sensing
   846 â”‚ â”‚                *   surface.
   847 â”‚ â”‚                */
   848 â”‚ â”‚               PROXIMITY_OUT,
   849 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   850 â”‚ â”‚                * the mouse has entered the window while a drag is in progress.
   851 â”‚ â”‚                */
   852 â”‚ â”‚               DRAG_ENTER,
   853 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   854 â”‚ â”‚                * the mouse has left the window while a drag is in progress.
   855 â”‚ â”‚                */
   856 â”‚ â”‚               DRAG_LEAVE,
   857 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   858 â”‚ â”‚                * the mouse has moved in the window while a drag is in
   859 â”‚ â”‚                *   progress.
   860 â”‚ â”‚                */
   861 â”‚ â”‚               DRAG_MOTION,
   862 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   863 â”‚ â”‚                * the status of the drag operation initiated by the window
   864 â”‚ â”‚                *   has changed.
   865 â”‚ â”‚                */
   866 â”‚ â”‚               DRAG_STATUS,
   867 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   868 â”‚ â”‚                * a drop operation onto the window has started.
   869 â”‚ â”‚                */
   870 â”‚ â”‚               DROP_START,
   871 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   872 â”‚ â”‚                * the drop operation initiated by the window has completed.
   873 â”‚ â”‚                */
   874 â”‚ â”‚               DROP_FINISHED,
   875 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   876 â”‚ â”‚                * a message has been received from another application.
   877 â”‚ â”‚                */
   878 â”‚ â”‚               CLIENT_EVENT,
   879 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   880 â”‚ â”‚                * the window visibility status has changed.
   881 â”‚ â”‚                */
   882 â”‚ â”‚               VISIBILITY_NOTIFY,
   883 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   884 â”‚ â”‚                * the scroll wheel was turned
   885 â”‚ â”‚                */
   886 â”‚ â”‚               SCROLL,
   887 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   888 â”‚ â”‚                * the state of a window has changed. See #GdkWindowState
   889 â”‚ â”‚                *   for the possible window states
   890 â”‚ â”‚                */
   891 â”‚ â”‚               WINDOW_STATE,
   892 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   893 â”‚ â”‚                * a setting has been modified.
   894 â”‚ â”‚                */
   895 â”‚ â”‚               SETTING,
   896 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   897 â”‚ â”‚                * the owner of a selection has changed. This event type
   898 â”‚ â”‚                *   was added in 2.6
   899 â”‚ â”‚                */
   900 â”‚ â”‚               OWNER_CHANGE,
   901 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   902 â”‚ â”‚                * a pointer or keyboard grab was broken. This event type
   903 â”‚ â”‚                *   was added in 2.8.
   904 â”‚ â”‚                */
   905 â”‚ â”‚               GRAB_BROKEN,
   906 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   907 â”‚ â”‚                * the content of the window has been changed. This event type
   908 â”‚ â”‚                *   was added in 2.14.
   909 â”‚ â”‚                */
   910 â”‚ â”‚               DAMAGE,
   911 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   912 â”‚ â”‚                * A new touch event sequence has just started. This event
   913 â”‚ â”‚                *   type was added in 3.4.
   914 â”‚ â”‚                */
   915 â”‚ â”‚               TOUCH_BEGIN,
   916 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   917 â”‚ â”‚                * A touch event sequence has been updated. This event type
   918 â”‚ â”‚                *   was added in 3.4.
   919 â”‚ â”‚                */
   920 â”‚ â”‚               TOUCH_UPDATE,
   921 â”‚ â”‚               /**
   922 â”‚ â”‚                * A touch event sequence has finished. This event type

  1564 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1565 â”‚ â”‚            * Specifies the current state of a touchpad gesture. All gestures are
  1566 â”‚ â”‚            * guaranteed to begin with an event with phase %GDK_TOUCHPAD_GESTURE_PHASE_BEGIN,
  1567 â”‚ â”‚            * followed by 0 or several events with phase %GDK_TOUCHPAD_GESTURE_PHASE_UPDATE.
  1568 â”‚ â”‚            *
  1569 â”‚ â”‚            * A finished gesture may have 2 possible outcomes, an event with phase
  1570 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_TOUCHPAD_GESTURE_PHASE_END will be emitted when the gesture is
  1571 â”‚ â”‚            * considered successful, this should be used as the hint to perform any
  1572 â”‚ â”‚            * permanent changes.
  1573 â”‚ â”‚            *
  1574 â”‚ â”‚            * Cancelled gestures may be so for a variety of reasons, due to hardware
  1575 â”‚ â”‚            * or the compositor, or due to the gesture recognition layers hinting the
  1576 â”‚ â”‚            * gesture did not finish resolutely (eg. a 3rd finger being added during
  1577 â”‚ â”‚            * a pinch gesture). In these cases, the last event will report the phase
  1578 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_TOUCHPAD_GESTURE_PHASE_CANCEL, this should be used as a hint
  1579 â”‚ â”‚            * to undo any visible/permanent changes that were done throughout the
  1580 â”‚ â”‚            * progress of the gesture.
  1581 â”‚ â”‚            *
  1582 â”‚ â”‚            * See also #GdkEventTouchpadSwipe and #GdkEventTouchpadPinch.
  1583 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1584 â”‚ â”‚

  1588 â”‚ â”‚            * followed by 0 or several events with phase %GDK_TOUCHPAD_GESTURE_PHASE_UPDATE.
  1589 â”‚ â”‚            *

  1609 â”‚ â”‚           enum TouchpadGesturePhase {

  1753 â”‚ â”‚   
  1754 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1755 â”‚ â”‚            * Describes the kind of window.
  1756 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1757 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace WindowType {
  1758 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<WindowType>;
  1759 â”‚ â”‚           }
  1760 â”‚ â”‚   
  1761 â”‚ â”‚           enum WindowType {
  1762 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1763 â”‚ â”‚                * root window; this window has no parent, covers the entire
  1764 â”‚ â”‚                *  screen, and is created by the window system
  1765 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1766 â”‚ â”‚               ROOT,
  1767 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1768 â”‚ â”‚                * toplevel window (used to implement #GtkWindow)
  1769 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1770 â”‚ â”‚               TOPLEVEL,
  1771 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1772 â”‚ â”‚                * child window (used to implement e.g. #GtkEntry)
  1773 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1774 â”‚ â”‚               CHILD,
  1775 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1776 â”‚ â”‚                * override redirect temporary window (used to implement
  1777 â”‚ â”‚                *  #GtkMenu)
  1778 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1779 â”‚ â”‚               TEMP,
  1780 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1781 â”‚ â”‚                * foreign window (see gdk_window_foreign_new())
  1782 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1783 â”‚ â”‚               FOREIGN,
  1784 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1785 â”‚ â”‚                * offscreen window (see
  1786 â”‚ â”‚                *  [Offscreen Windows][OFFSCREEN-WINDOWS]). Since 2.18
  1787 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1788 â”‚ â”‚               OFFSCREEN,
  1789 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1790 â”‚ â”‚                * subsurface-based window; This window is visually
  1791 â”‚ â”‚                *  tied to a toplevel, and is moved/stacked with it. Currently this window
  1792 â”‚ â”‚                *  type is only implemented in Wayland. Since 3.14
  1793 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1794 â”‚ â”‚               SUBSURFACE,
  1795 â”‚ â”‚           }
  1796 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1797 â”‚ â”‚            * These are hints for the window manager that indicate what type of function
  1798 â”‚ â”‚            * the window has. The window manager can use this when determining decoration
  1799 â”‚ â”‚            * and behaviour of the window. The hint must be set before mapping the window.
  1800 â”‚ â”‚            *
  1801 â”‚ â”‚            * See the [Extended Window Manager Hints](http://www.freedesktop.org/Standards/wm-spec)
  1802 â”‚ â”‚            * specification for more details about window types.
  1803 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1804 â”‚ â”‚   
  1805 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1806 â”‚ â”‚            * These are hints for the window manager that indicate what type of function
  1807 â”‚ â”‚            * the window has. The window manager can use this when determining decoration
  1808 â”‚ â”‚            * and behaviour of the window. The hint must be set before mapping the window.
  1809 â”‚ â”‚            *
  1810 â”‚ â”‚            * See the [Extended Window Manager Hints](http://www.freedesktop.org/Standards/wm-spec)
  1811 â”‚ â”‚            * specification for more details about window types.
  1812 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1813 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace WindowTypeHint {
  1814 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<WindowTypeHint>;
  1815 â”‚ â”‚           }
  1816 â”‚ â”‚   
  1817 â”‚ â”‚           enum WindowTypeHint {
  1818 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1819 â”‚ â”‚                * Normal toplevel window.
  1820 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1821 â”‚ â”‚               NORMAL,
  1822 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1823 â”‚ â”‚                * Dialog window.
  1824 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1825 â”‚ â”‚               DIALOG,
  1826 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1827 â”‚ â”‚                * Window used to implement a menu; GTK+ uses
  1828 â”‚ â”‚                *  this hint only for torn-off menus, see #GtkTearoffMenuItem.
  1829 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1830 â”‚ â”‚               MENU,
  1831 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1832 â”‚ â”‚                * Window used to implement toolbars.
  1833 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1834 â”‚ â”‚               TOOLBAR,
  1835 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1836 â”‚ â”‚                * Window used to display a splash
  1837 â”‚ â”‚                *  screen during application startup.
  1838 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1839 â”‚ â”‚               SPLASHSCREEN,
  1840 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1841 â”‚ â”‚                * Utility windows which are not detached
  1842 â”‚ â”‚                *  toolbars or dialogs.
  1843 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1844 â”‚ â”‚               UTILITY,
  1845 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1846 â”‚ â”‚                * Used for creating dock or panel windows.
  1847 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1848 â”‚ â”‚               DOCK,
  1849 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1850 â”‚ â”‚                * Used for creating the desktop background
  1851 â”‚ â”‚                *  window.
  1852 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1853 â”‚ â”‚               DESKTOP,
  1854 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1855 â”‚ â”‚                * A menu that belongs to a menubar.
  1856 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1857 â”‚ â”‚               DROPDOWN_MENU,
  1858 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1859 â”‚ â”‚                * A menu that does not belong to a menubar,
  1860 â”‚ â”‚                *  e.g. a context menu.
  1861 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1862 â”‚ â”‚               POPUP_MENU,
  1863 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1864 â”‚ â”‚                * A tooltip.
  1865 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1866 â”‚ â”‚               TOOLTIP,
  1867 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1868 â”‚ â”‚                * A notification - typically a â€œbubbleâ€
  1869 â”‚ â”‚                *  that belongs to a status icon.
  1870 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1871 â”‚ â”‚               NOTIFICATION,
  1872 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1873 â”‚ â”‚                * A popup from a combo box.
  1874 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1875 â”‚ â”‚               COMBO,
  1876 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1877 â”‚ â”‚                * A window that is used to implement a DND cursor.
  1878 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1879 â”‚ â”‚               DND,
  1880 â”‚ â”‚           }
  1881 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1882 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_OUTPUT` windows are the standard kind of window you might expect.
  1883 â”‚ â”‚            * Such windows receive events and are also displayed on screen.
  1884 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_ONLY` windows are invisible; they are usually placed above other
  1885 â”‚ â”‚            * windows in order to trap or filter the events. You canâ€™t draw on
  1886 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_ONLY` windows.
  1887 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1888 â”‚ â”‚   
  1889 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  1890 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_OUTPUT` windows are the standard kind of window you might expect.
  1891 â”‚ â”‚            * Such windows receive events and are also displayed on screen.
  1892 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_ONLY` windows are invisible; they are usually placed above other
  1893 â”‚ â”‚            * windows in order to trap or filter the events. You canâ€™t draw on
  1894 â”‚ â”‚            * `GDK_INPUT_ONLY` windows.
  1895 â”‚ â”‚            */
  1896 â”‚ â”‚           export namespace WindowWindowClass {
  1897 â”‚ â”‚               export const $gtype: GObject.GType<WindowWindowClass>;
  1898 â”‚ â”‚           }
  1899 â”‚ â”‚

  1902 â”‚ â”‚                * window for graphics and events
  1903 â”‚ â”‚                */

  1905 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  1906 â”‚ â”‚                * window for events only
  1907 â”‚ â”‚                */
  1908 â”‚ â”‚               INPUT_ONLY,
  1909 â”‚ â”‚           }

  4280 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  4281 â”‚ â”‚            * This is the main way to draw GL content in GTK+. It takes a render buffer ID
  4282 â”‚ â”‚            * (`source_type` == #GL_RENDERBUFFER) or a texture id (`source_type` == #GL_TEXTURE)
  4283 â”‚ â”‚            * and draws it onto `cr` with an OVER operation, respecting the current clip.
  4284 â”‚ â”‚            * The top left corner of the rectangle specified by `x,` `y,` `width` and `height`
  4285 â”‚ â”‚            * will be drawn at the current (0,0) position of the cairo_t.
  4286 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4287 â”‚ â”‚            * This will work for *all* cairo_t, as long as `window` is realized, but the
  4288 â”‚ â”‚            * fallback implementation that reads back the pixels from the buffer may be
  4289 â”‚ â”‚            * used in the general case. In the case of direct drawing to a window with
  4290 â”‚ â”‚            * no special effects applied to `cr` it will however use a more efficient
  4291 â”‚ â”‚            * approach.
  4292 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4293 â”‚ â”‚            * For #GL_RENDERBUFFER the code will always fall back to software for buffers
  4294 â”‚ â”‚            * with alpha components, so make sure you use #GL_TEXTURE if using alpha.
  4295 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4296 â”‚ â”‚            * Calling this may change the current GL context.
  4297 â”‚ â”‚            * @param cr a cairo context
  4298 â”‚ â”‚            * @param window The window we're rendering for (not necessarily into)
  4299 â”‚ â”‚            * @param source The GL ID of the source buffer
  4300 â”‚ â”‚            * @param source_type The type of the @source
  4301 â”‚ â”‚            * @param buffer_scale The scale-factor that the @source buffer is allocated for
  4302 â”‚ â”‚            * @param x The source x position in @source to start copying from in GL coordinates
  4303 â”‚ â”‚            * @param y The source y position in @source to start copying from in GL coordinates
  4304 â”‚ â”‚            * @param width The width of the region to draw
  4305 â”‚ â”‚            * @param height The height of the region to draw
  4306 â”‚ â”‚            */
  4307 â”‚ â”‚           function cairo_draw_from_gl(
  4308 â”‚ â”‚               cr: cairo.Context,
  4309 â”‚ â”‚               window: Window,
  4310 â”‚ â”‚               source: number,
  4311 â”‚ â”‚               source_type: number,
  4312 â”‚ â”‚               buffer_scale: number,
  4313 â”‚ â”‚               x: number,

  4604 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  4605 â”‚ â”‚            * Removes an error trap pushed with gdk_error_trap_push().
  4606 â”‚ â”‚            * May block until an error has been definitively received
  4607 â”‚ â”‚            * or not received from the X server. gdk_error_trap_pop_ignored()
  4608 â”‚ â”‚            * is preferred if you donâ€™t need to know whether an error
  4609 â”‚ â”‚            * occurred, because it never has to block. If you don't
  4610 â”‚ â”‚            * need the return value of gdk_error_trap_pop(), use
  4611 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_error_trap_pop_ignored().
  4612 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4613 â”‚ â”‚            * Prior to GDK 3.0, this function would not automatically
  4614 â”‚ â”‚            * sync for you, so you had to gdk_flush() if your last
  4615 â”‚ â”‚            * call to Xlib was not a blocking round trip.
  4616 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns X error code or 0 on success
  4617 â”‚ â”‚            */
  4618 â”‚ â”‚           function error_trap_pop(): number;
  4619 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  4620 â”‚ â”‚            * Removes an error trap pushed with gdk_error_trap_push(), but
  4621 â”‚ â”‚            * without bothering to wait and see whether an error occurred.  If an
  4622 â”‚ â”‚            * error arrives later asynchronously that was triggered while the
  4623 â”‚ â”‚            * trap was pushed, that error will be ignored.
  4624 â”‚ â”‚            */
  4625 â”‚ â”‚           function error_trap_pop_ignored(): void;
  4626 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  4627 â”‚ â”‚            * This function allows X errors to be trapped instead of the normal
  4628 â”‚ â”‚            * behavior of exiting the application. It should only be used if it
  4629 â”‚ â”‚            * is not possible to avoid the X error in any other way. Errors are
  4630 â”‚ â”‚            * ignored on all #GdkDisplay currently known to the
  4631 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkDisplayManager. If you donâ€™t care which error happens and just
  4632 â”‚ â”‚            * want to ignore everything, pop with gdk_error_trap_pop_ignored().
  4633 â”‚ â”‚            * If you need the error code, use gdk_error_trap_pop() which may have
  4634 â”‚ â”‚            * to block and wait for the error to arrive from the X server.
  4635 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4636 â”‚ â”‚            * This API exists on all platforms but only does anything on X.
  4637 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4638 â”‚ â”‚            * You can use gdk_x11_display_error_trap_push() to ignore errors
  4639 â”‚ â”‚            * on only a single display.
  4640 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4641 â”‚ â”‚            * ## Trapping an X error
  4642 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4643 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4644 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  4645 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_error_trap_push ();
  4646 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4647 â”‚ â”‚            *  // ... Call the X function which may cause an error here ...
  4648 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4649 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4650 â”‚ â”‚            * if (gdk_error_trap_pop ())
  4651 â”‚ â”‚            *  {
  4652 â”‚ â”‚            *    // ... Handle the error here ...
  4653 â”‚ â”‚            *  }
  4654 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  4655 â”‚ â”‚            *
  4656 â”‚ â”‚            */
  4657 â”‚ â”‚           function error_trap_push(): void;

  4801 â”‚ â”‚            * Grabs the keyboard so that all events are passed to this

  5000 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5001 â”‚ â”‚            * Transfers image data from a #cairo_surface_t and converts it to an RGB(A)
  5002 â”‚ â”‚            * representation inside a #GdkPixbuf. This allows you to efficiently read
  5003 â”‚ â”‚            * individual pixels from cairo surfaces. For #GdkWindows, use
  5004 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_pixbuf_get_from_window() instead.
  5005 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5006 â”‚ â”‚            * This function will create an RGB pixbuf with 8 bits per channel.
  5007 â”‚ â”‚            * The pixbuf will contain an alpha channel if the `surface` contains one.
  5008 â”‚ â”‚            * @param surface surface to copy from
  5009 â”‚ â”‚            * @param src_x Source X coordinate within @surface
  5010 â”‚ â”‚            * @param src_y Source Y coordinate within @surface
  5011 â”‚ â”‚            * @param width Width in pixels of region to get
  5012 â”‚ â”‚            * @param height Height in pixels of region to get
  5013 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns A newly-created pixbuf with a     reference count of 1, or %NULL on error
  5014 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5015 â”‚ â”‚           function pixbuf_get_from_surface(
  5016 â”‚ â”‚               surface: cairo.Surface,
  5017 â”‚ â”‚               src_x: number,
  5018 â”‚ â”‚               src_y: number,
  5019 â”‚ â”‚               width: number,
  5020 â”‚ â”‚               height: number,
  5021 â”‚ â”‚           ): GdkPixbuf.Pixbuf | null;
  5022 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5023 â”‚ â”‚            * Transfers image data from a #GdkWindow and converts it to an RGB(A)
  5024 â”‚ â”‚            * representation inside a #GdkPixbuf.
  5025 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5026 â”‚ â”‚            * In other words, copies image data from a server-side drawable to a
  5027 â”‚ â”‚            * client-side RGB(A) buffer. This allows you to efficiently read
  5028 â”‚ â”‚            * individual pixels on the client side.
  5029 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5030 â”‚ â”‚            * This function will create an RGB pixbuf with 8 bits per channel with
  5031 â”‚ â”‚            * the size specified by the `width` and `height` arguments scaled by the
  5032 â”‚ â”‚            * scale factor of `window`. The pixbuf will contain an alpha channel if
  5033 â”‚ â”‚            * the `window` contains one.
  5034 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5035 â”‚ â”‚            * If the window is off the screen, then there is no image data in the
  5036 â”‚ â”‚            * obscured/offscreen regions to be placed in the pixbuf. The contents of
  5037 â”‚ â”‚            * portions of the pixbuf corresponding to the offscreen region are
  5038 â”‚ â”‚            * undefined.
  5039 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5040 â”‚ â”‚            * If the window youâ€™re obtaining data from is partially obscured by
  5041 â”‚ â”‚            * other windows, then the contents of the pixbuf areas corresponding
  5042 â”‚ â”‚            * to the obscured regions are undefined.
  5043 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5044 â”‚ â”‚            * If the window is not mapped (typically because itâ€™s iconified/minimized
  5045 â”‚ â”‚            * or not on the current workspace), then %NULL will be returned.
  5046 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5047 â”‚ â”‚            * If memory canâ€™t be allocated for the return value, %NULL will be returned
  5048 â”‚ â”‚            * instead.
  5049 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5050 â”‚ â”‚            * In short, there are several ways this function can fail, and if it fails
  5051 â”‚ â”‚            * it returns %NULL; so check the return value.
  5052 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5053 â”‚ â”‚            * You should rarely, if ever, need to call this function.
  5054 â”‚ â”‚            * @param window Source window
  5055 â”‚ â”‚            * @param src_x Source X coordinate within @window
  5056 â”‚ â”‚            * @param src_y Source Y coordinate within @window
  5057 â”‚ â”‚            * @param width Width in pixels of region to get
  5058 â”‚ â”‚            * @param height Height in pixels of region to get
  5059 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns A newly-created pixbuf with a   reference count of 1, or %NULL on error
  5060 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5061 â”‚ â”‚           function pixbuf_get_from_window(
  5062 â”‚ â”‚               window: Window,
  5063 â”‚ â”‚               src_x: number,
  5064 â”‚ â”‚               src_y: number,
  5065 â”‚ â”‚               width: number,
  5066 â”‚ â”‚               height: number,
  5067 â”‚ â”‚           ): GdkPixbuf.Pixbuf | null;
  5068 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5069 â”‚ â”‚            * Grabs the pointer (usually a mouse) so that all events are passed to this
  5070 â”‚ â”‚            * application until the pointer is ungrabbed with gdk_pointer_ungrab(), or
  5071 â”‚ â”‚            * the grab window becomes unviewable.
  5072 â”‚ â”‚            * This overrides any previous pointer grab by this client.
  5073 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5074 â”‚ â”‚            * Pointer grabs are used for operations which need complete control over mouse
  5075 â”‚ â”‚            * events, even if the mouse leaves the application.
  5076 â”‚ â”‚            * For example in GTK+ it is used for Drag and Drop, for dragging the handle in
  5077 â”‚ â”‚            * the #GtkHPaned and #GtkVPaned widgets.
  5078 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5079 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that if the event mask of an X window has selected both button press and
  5080 â”‚ â”‚            * button release events, then a button press event will cause an automatic
  5081 â”‚ â”‚            * pointer grab until the button is released.
  5082 â”‚ â”‚            * X does this automatically since most applications expect to receive button
  5083 â”‚ â”‚            * press and release events in pairs.
  5084 â”‚ â”‚            * It is equivalent to a pointer grab on the window with `owner_events` set to
  5085 â”‚ â”‚            * %TRUE.
  5086 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5087 â”‚ â”‚            * If you set up anything at the time you take the grab that needs to be cleaned
  5088 â”‚ â”‚            * up when the grab ends, you should handle the #GdkEventGrabBroken events that
  5089 â”‚ â”‚            * are emitted when the grab ends unvoluntarily.
  5090 â”‚ â”‚            * @param window the #GdkWindow which will own the grab (the grab window).
  5091 â”‚ â”‚            * @param owner_events if %FALSE then all pointer events are reported with respect to                @window and are only reported if selected by @event_mask. If %TRUE then pointer                events for this application are reported as normal, but pointer events outside                this application are reported with respect to @window and only if selected by                @event_mask. In either mode, unreported events are discarded.
  5092 â”‚ â”‚            * @param event_mask specifies the event mask, which is used in accordance with              @owner_events. Note that only pointer events (i.e. button and motion events)              may be selected.
  5093 â”‚ â”‚            * @param confine_to If non-%NULL, the pointer will be confined to this              window during the grab. If the pointer is outside @confine_to, it will              automatically be moved to the closest edge of @confine_to and enter              and leave events will be generated as necessary.
  5094 â”‚ â”‚            * @param cursor the cursor to display while the grab is active. If this is %NULL then          the normal cursors are used for @window and its descendants, and the cursor          for @window is used for all other windows.
  5095 â”‚ â”‚            * @param time_ the timestamp of the event which led to this pointer grab. This usually         comes from a #GdkEventButton struct, though %GDK_CURRENT_TIME can be used if         the time isnâ€™t known.
  5096 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns %GDK_GRAB_SUCCESS if the grab was successful.
  5097 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5098 â”‚ â”‚           function pointer_grab(
  5099 â”‚ â”‚               window: Window,
  5100 â”‚ â”‚               owner_events: boolean,
  5101 â”‚ â”‚               event_mask: EventMask | null,
  5102 â”‚ â”‚               confine_to: Window | null,
  5103 â”‚ â”‚               cursor: Cursor | null,
  5104 â”‚ â”‚               time_: number,
  5105 â”‚ â”‚           ): GrabStatus;
  5106 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5107 â”‚ â”‚            * Returns %TRUE if the pointer on the default display is currently
  5108 â”‚ â”‚            * grabbed by this application.
  5109 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5110 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that this does not take the inmplicit pointer grab on button
  5111 â”‚ â”‚            * presses into account.
  5112 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns %TRUE if the pointer is currently grabbed by this application.
  5113 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5114 â”‚ â”‚           function pointer_is_grabbed(): boolean;
  5115 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5116 â”‚ â”‚            * Ungrabs the pointer on the default display, if it is grabbed by this
  5117 â”‚ â”‚            * application.
  5118 â”‚ â”‚            * @param time_ a timestamp from a #GdkEvent, or %GDK_CURRENT_TIME if no  timestamp is available.
  5119 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5120 â”‚ â”‚           function pointer_ungrab(time_: number): void;
  5121 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5122 â”‚ â”‚            * Prepare for parsing command line arguments for GDK. This is not
  5123 â”‚ â”‚            * public API and should not be used in application code.

  5127 â”‚ â”‚            * Deletes a property from a window.

  5129 â”‚ â”‚            * @param property the property to delete

  5132 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5133 â”‚ â”‚            * Retrieves a portion of the contents of a property. If the
  5134 â”‚ â”‚            * property does not exist, then the function returns %FALSE,
  5135 â”‚ â”‚            * and %GDK_NONE will be stored in `actual_property_type`.
  5136 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5137 â”‚ â”‚            * The XGetWindowProperty() function that gdk_property_get()
  5138 â”‚ â”‚            * uses has a very confusing and complicated set of semantics.
  5139 â”‚ â”‚            * Unfortunately, gdk_property_get() makes the situation
  5140 â”‚ â”‚            * worse instead of better (the semantics should be considered
  5141 â”‚ â”‚            * undefined), and also prints warnings to stderr in cases where it
  5142 â”‚ â”‚            * should return a useful error to the program. You are advised to use
  5143 â”‚ â”‚            * XGetWindowProperty() directly until a replacement function for
  5144 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_property_get() is provided.
  5145 â”‚ â”‚            * @param window a #GdkWindow
  5146 â”‚ â”‚            * @param property the property to retrieve
  5147 â”‚ â”‚            * @param type the desired property type, or %GDK_NONE, if any type of data   is acceptable. If this does not match the actual   type, then @actual_format and @actual_length will   be filled in, a warning will be printed to stderr   and no data will be returned.
  5148 â”‚ â”‚            * @param offset the offset into the property at which to begin   retrieving data, in 4 byte units.
  5149 â”‚ â”‚            * @param length the length of the data to retrieve in bytes.  Data is   considered to be retrieved in 4 byte chunks, so @length   will be rounded up to the next highest 4 byte boundary   (so be careful not to pass a value that might overflow   when rounded up).
  5150 â”‚ â”‚            * @param pdelete if %TRUE, delete the property after retrieving the   data.
  5151 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns %TRUE if data was successfully received and stored   in @data, otherwise %FALSE.
  5152 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5153 â”‚ â”‚           function property_get(
  5154 â”‚ â”‚               window: Window,
  5155 â”‚ â”‚               property: Atom,
  5156 â”‚ â”‚               type: Atom,
  5157 â”‚ â”‚               offset: number,
  5158 â”‚ â”‚               length: number,
  5159 â”‚ â”‚               pdelete: number,
  5160 â”‚ â”‚           ): [boolean, Atom, number, Uint8Array];
  5161 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5162 â”‚ â”‚            * This function returns the available bit depths for the default
  5163 â”‚ â”‚            * screen. Itâ€™s equivalent to listing the visuals
  5164 â”‚ â”‚            * (gdk_list_visuals()) and then looking at the depth field in each

  5267 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5268 â”‚ â”‚            * Sets a list of backends that GDK should try to use.
  5269 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5270 â”‚ â”‚            * This can be be useful if your application does not
  5271 â”‚ â”‚            * work with certain GDK backends.
  5272 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5273 â”‚ â”‚            * By default, GDK tries all included backends.
  5274 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5275 â”‚ â”‚            * For example,
  5276 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5277 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  5278 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_set_allowed_backends ("wayland,quartz,*");
  5279 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  5280 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5281 â”‚ â”‚            * instructs GDK to try the Wayland backend first,
  5282 â”‚ â”‚            * followed by the Quartz backend, and then all
  5283 â”‚ â”‚            * others.
  5284 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5285 â”‚ â”‚            * If the `GDK_BACKEND` environment variable
  5286 â”‚ â”‚            * is set, it determines what backends are tried in what
  5287 â”‚ â”‚            * order, while still respecting the set of allowed backends
  5288 â”‚ â”‚            * that are specified by this function.
  5289 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5290 â”‚ â”‚            * The possible backend names are x11, win32, quartz,
  5291 â”‚ â”‚            * broadway, wayland. You can also include a * in the
  5292 â”‚ â”‚            * list to try all remaining backends.
  5293 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5294 â”‚ â”‚            * This call must happen prior to gdk_display_open(),
  5295 â”‚ â”‚            * gtk_init(), gtk_init_with_args() or gtk_init_check()
  5296 â”‚ â”‚            * in order to take effect.
  5297 â”‚ â”‚            * @param backends a comma-separated list of backends
  5298 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5299 â”‚ â”‚           function set_allowed_backends(backends: string): void;
  5300 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5301 â”‚ â”‚            * Set the double click time for the default display. See

  5303 â”‚ â”‚            * See also gdk_display_set_double_click_distance().
  5304 â”‚ â”‚            * Applications should not set this, it is a

  5349 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5350 â”‚ â”‚            * This function is intended to be used in GTK+ test programs.
  5351 â”‚ â”‚            * It will warp the mouse pointer to the given (`x,``y)` coordinates
  5352 â”‚ â”‚            * within `window` and simulate a button press or release event.
  5353 â”‚ â”‚            * Because the mouse pointer needs to be warped to the target
  5354 â”‚ â”‚            * location, use of this function outside of test programs that

  5356 â”‚ â”‚            * recommended.

  5360 â”‚ â”‚            * function to call which will generate a button press event followed

  5368 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns whether all actions necessary for a button event simulation     were carried out successfully
  5369 â”‚ â”‚            */

  5375 â”‚ â”‚               modifiers: ModifierType | null,
  5376 â”‚ â”‚               button_pressrelease: EventType | null,
  5377 â”‚ â”‚           ): boolean;
  5378 â”‚ â”‚           /**

  5411 â”‚ â”‚           /**

  5426 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5427 â”‚ â”‚            * Adds a function to be called whenever there are no higher priority
  5428 â”‚ â”‚            * events pending.  If the function returns %FALSE it is automatically
  5429 â”‚ â”‚            * removed from the list of event sources and will not be called again.
  5430 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5431 â”‚ â”‚            * This variant of g_idle_add_full() calls `function` with the GDK lock
  5432 â”‚ â”‚            * held. It can be thought of a MT-safe version for GTK+ widgets for the
  5433 â”‚ â”‚            * following use case, where you have to worry about idle_callback()
  5434 â”‚ â”‚            * running in thread A and accessing `self` after it has been finalized
  5435 â”‚ â”‚            * in thread B:
  5436 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5437 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5438 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  5439 â”‚ â”‚            * static gboolean
  5440 â”‚ â”‚            * idle_callback (gpointer data)
  5441 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5442 â”‚ â”‚            *    // gdk_threads_enter(); would be needed for g_idle_add()
  5443 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5444 â”‚ â”‚            *    SomeWidget *self = data;
  5445 â”‚ â”‚            *    // do stuff with self
  5446 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5447 â”‚ â”‚            *    self->idle_id = 0;
  5448 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5449 â”‚ â”‚            *    // gdk_threads_leave(); would be needed for g_idle_add()
  5450 â”‚ â”‚            *    return FALSE;
  5451 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5452 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5453 â”‚ â”‚            * static void
  5454 â”‚ â”‚            * some_widget_do_stuff_later (SomeWidget *self)
  5455 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5456 â”‚ â”‚            *    self->idle_id = gdk_threads_add_idle (idle_callback, self)
  5457 â”‚ â”‚            *    // using g_idle_add() here would require thread protection in the callback
  5458 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5459 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5460 â”‚ â”‚            * static void
  5461 â”‚ â”‚            * some_widget_finalize (GObject *object)
  5462 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5463 â”‚ â”‚            *    SomeWidget *self = SOME_WIDGET (object);
  5464 â”‚ â”‚            *    if (self->idle_id)
  5465 â”‚ â”‚            *      g_source_remove (self->idle_id);
  5466 â”‚ â”‚            *    G_OBJECT_CLASS (parent_class)->finalize (object);
  5467 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5468 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  5469 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5470 â”‚ â”‚            * @param priority the priority of the idle source. Typically this will be in the            range between #G_PRIORITY_DEFAULT_IDLE and #G_PRIORITY_HIGH_IDLE
  5471 â”‚ â”‚            * @param _function function to call
  5472 â”‚ â”‚            * @param notify function to call when the idle is removed, or %NULL
  5473 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns the ID (greater than 0) of the event source.
  5474 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5475 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_add_idle(
  5476 â”‚ â”‚               priority: number,
  5477 â”‚ â”‚               _function: GLib.SourceFunc,
  5478 â”‚ â”‚               notify?: GLib.DestroyNotify | null,
  5479 â”‚ â”‚           ): number;
  5480 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5481 â”‚ â”‚            * Sets a function to be called at regular intervals holding the GDK lock,
  5482 â”‚ â”‚            * with the given priority.  The function is called repeatedly until it
  5483 â”‚ â”‚            * returns %FALSE, at which point the timeout is automatically destroyed
  5484 â”‚ â”‚            * and the function will not be called again.  The `notify` function is
  5485 â”‚ â”‚            * called when the timeout is destroyed.  The first call to the
  5486 â”‚ â”‚            * function will be at the end of the first `interval`.
  5487 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5488 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that timeout functions may be delayed, due to the processing of other
  5489 â”‚ â”‚            * event sources. Thus they should not be relied on for precise timing.
  5490 â”‚ â”‚            * After each call to the timeout function, the time of the next
  5491 â”‚ â”‚            * timeout is recalculated based on the current time and the given interval
  5492 â”‚ â”‚            * (it does not try to â€œcatch upâ€ time lost in delays).
  5493 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5494 â”‚ â”‚            * This variant of g_timeout_add_full() can be thought of a MT-safe version
  5495 â”‚ â”‚            * for GTK+ widgets for the following use case:
  5496 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5497 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5498 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  5499 â”‚ â”‚            * static gboolean timeout_callback (gpointer data)
  5500 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5501 â”‚ â”‚            *    SomeWidget *self = data;
  5502 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5503 â”‚ â”‚            *    // do stuff with self
  5504 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5505 â”‚ â”‚            *    self->timeout_id = 0;
  5506 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5507 â”‚ â”‚            *    return G_SOURCE_REMOVE;
  5508 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5509 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5510 â”‚ â”‚            * static void some_widget_do_stuff_later (SomeWidget *self)
  5511 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5512 â”‚ â”‚            *    self->timeout_id = g_timeout_add (timeout_callback, self)
  5513 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5514 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5515 â”‚ â”‚            * static void some_widget_finalize (GObject *object)
  5516 â”‚ â”‚            * {
  5517 â”‚ â”‚            *    SomeWidget *self = SOME_WIDGET (object);
  5518 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5519 â”‚ â”‚            *    if (self->timeout_id)
  5520 â”‚ â”‚            *      g_source_remove (self->timeout_id);
  5521 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5522 â”‚ â”‚            *    G_OBJECT_CLASS (parent_class)->finalize (object);
  5523 â”‚ â”‚            * }
  5524 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  5525 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5526 â”‚ â”‚            * @param priority the priority of the timeout source. Typically this will be in the            range between #G_PRIORITY_DEFAULT_IDLE and #G_PRIORITY_HIGH_IDLE.
  5527 â”‚ â”‚            * @param interval the time between calls to the function, in milliseconds             (1/1000ths of a second)
  5528 â”‚ â”‚            * @param _function function to call
  5529 â”‚ â”‚            * @param notify function to call when the timeout is removed, or %NULL
  5530 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns the ID (greater than 0) of the event source.
  5531 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5532 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_add_timeout(
  5533 â”‚ â”‚               priority: number,
  5534 â”‚ â”‚               interval: number,
  5535 â”‚ â”‚               _function: GLib.SourceFunc,
  5536 â”‚ â”‚               notify?: GLib.DestroyNotify | null,
  5537 â”‚ â”‚           ): number;
  5538 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5539 â”‚ â”‚            * A variant of gdk_threads_add_timeout_full() with second-granularity.
  5540 â”‚ â”‚            * See g_timeout_add_seconds_full() for a discussion of why it is
  5541 â”‚ â”‚            * a good idea to use this function if you donâ€™t need finer granularity.
  5542 â”‚ â”‚            * @param priority the priority of the timeout source. Typically this will be in the            range between #G_PRIORITY_DEFAULT_IDLE and #G_PRIORITY_HIGH_IDLE.
  5543 â”‚ â”‚            * @param interval the time between calls to the function, in seconds
  5544 â”‚ â”‚            * @param _function function to call
  5545 â”‚ â”‚            * @param notify function to call when the timeout is removed, or %NULL
  5546 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns the ID (greater than 0) of the event source.
  5547 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5548 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_add_timeout_seconds(
  5549 â”‚ â”‚               priority: number,
  5550 â”‚ â”‚               interval: number,
  5551 â”‚ â”‚               _function: GLib.SourceFunc,
  5552 â”‚ â”‚               notify?: GLib.DestroyNotify | null,
  5553 â”‚ â”‚           ): number;
  5554 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5555 â”‚ â”‚            * This function marks the beginning of a critical section in which
  5556 â”‚ â”‚            * GDK and GTK+ functions can be called safely and without causing race
  5557 â”‚ â”‚            * conditions. Only one thread at a time can be in such a critial
  5558 â”‚ â”‚            * section.
  5559 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5560 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_enter(): void;
  5561 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5562 â”‚ â”‚            * Initializes GDK so that it can be used from multiple threads
  5563 â”‚ â”‚            * in conjunction with gdk_threads_enter() and gdk_threads_leave().
  5564 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5565 â”‚ â”‚            * This call must be made before any use of the main loop from
  5566 â”‚ â”‚            * GTK+; to be safe, call it before gtk_init().
  5567 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5568 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_init(): void;
  5569 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5570 â”‚ â”‚            * Leaves a critical region begun with gdk_threads_enter().
  5571 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5572 â”‚ â”‚           function threads_leave(): void;
  5573 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5574 â”‚ â”‚            * Convert from a ISO10646 character to a key symbol.
  5575 â”‚ â”‚            * @param wc a ISO10646 encoded character
  5576 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns the corresponding GDK key symbol, if one exists.               or, if there is no corresponding symbol,               wc | 0x01000000
  5577 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5578 â”‚ â”‚           function unicode_to_keyval(wc: number): number;
  5579 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5580 â”‚ â”‚            * Converts an UTF-8 string into the best possible representation
  5581 â”‚ â”‚            * as a STRING. The representation of characters not in STRING
  5582 â”‚ â”‚            * is not specified; it may be as pseudo-escape sequences
  5583 â”‚ â”‚            * \x{ABCD}, or it may be in some other form of approximation.
  5584 â”‚ â”‚            * @param str a UTF-8 string
  5585 â”‚ â”‚            * @returns the newly-allocated string, or %NULL if the          conversion failed. (It should not fail for any properly          formed UTF-8 string unless system limits like memory or          file descriptors are exceeded.)
  5586 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5587 â”‚ â”‚           function utf8_to_string_target(str: string): string | null;

  5603 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5604 â”‚ â”‚            * Positioning hints for aligning a window relative to a rectangle.
  5605 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5606 â”‚ â”‚            * These hints determine how the window should be positioned in the case that
  5607 â”‚ â”‚            * the window would fall off-screen if placed in its ideal position.
  5608 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5609 â”‚ â”‚            * For example, %GDK_ANCHOR_FLIP_X will replace %GDK_GRAVITY_NORTH_WEST with
  5610 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_GRAVITY_NORTH_EAST and vice versa if the window extends beyond the left
  5611 â”‚ â”‚            * or right edges of the monitor.
  5612 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5613 â”‚ â”‚            * If %GDK_ANCHOR_SLIDE_X is set, the window can be shifted horizontally to fit
  5614 â”‚ â”‚            * on-screen. If %GDK_ANCHOR_RESIZE_X is set, the window can be shrunken
  5615 â”‚ â”‚            * horizontally to fit.
  5616 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5617 â”‚ â”‚            * In general, when multiple flags are set, flipping should take precedence over
  5618 â”‚ â”‚            * sliding, which should take precedence over resizing.
  5619 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5620 â”‚ â”‚

  5741 â”‚ â”‚   
  5742 â”‚ â”‚           enum DragAction {
  5743 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5744 â”‚ â”‚                * Means nothing, and should not be used.
  5745 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5746 â”‚ â”‚               DEFAULT,
  5747 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5748 â”‚ â”‚                * Copy the data.
  5749 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5750 â”‚ â”‚               COPY,
  5751 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5752 â”‚ â”‚                * Move the data, i.e. first copy it, then delete
  5753 â”‚ â”‚                *  it from the source using the DELETE target of the X selection protocol.
  5754 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5755 â”‚ â”‚               MOVE,
  5756 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5757 â”‚ â”‚                * Add a link to the data. Note that this is only
  5758 â”‚ â”‚                *  useful if source and destination agree on what it means.
  5759 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5760 â”‚ â”‚               LINK,
  5761 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5762 â”‚ â”‚                * Special action which tells the source that the
  5763 â”‚ â”‚                *  destination will do something that the source doesnâ€™t understand.
  5764 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5765 â”‚ â”‚               PRIVATE,
  5766 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  5767 â”‚ â”‚                * Ask the user what to do with the data.
  5768 â”‚ â”‚                */
  5769 â”‚ â”‚               ASK,
  5770 â”‚ â”‚           }
  5771 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5772 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of bit-flags to indicate which events a window is to receive.
  5773 â”‚ â”‚            * Most of these masks map onto one or more of the #GdkEventType event types
  5774 â”‚ â”‚            * above.
  5775 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5776 â”‚ â”‚            * See the [input handling overview][chap-input-handling] for details of
  5777 â”‚ â”‚            * [event masks][event-masks] and [event propagation][event-propagation].
  5778 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5779 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_POINTER_MOTION_HINT_MASK is deprecated. It is a special mask
  5780 â”‚ â”‚            * to reduce the number of %GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY events received. When using
  5781 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_POINTER_MOTION_HINT_MASK, fewer %GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY events will
  5782 â”‚ â”‚            * be sent, some of which are marked as a hint (the is_hint member is
  5783 â”‚ â”‚            * %TRUE). To receive more motion events after a motion hint event,
  5784 â”‚ â”‚            * the application needs to asks for more, by calling
  5785 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_event_request_motions().
  5786 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5787 â”‚ â”‚            * Since GTK 3.8, motion events are already compressed by default, independent
  5788 â”‚ â”‚            * of this mechanism. This compression can be disabled with
  5789 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_window_set_event_compression(). See the documentation of that function
  5790 â”‚ â”‚            * for details.
  5791 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5792 â”‚ â”‚            * If %GDK_TOUCH_MASK is enabled, the window will receive touch events
  5793 â”‚ â”‚            * from touch-enabled devices. Those will come as sequences of #GdkEventTouch
  5794 â”‚ â”‚            * with type %GDK_TOUCH_UPDATE, enclosed by two events with
  5795 â”‚ â”‚            * type %GDK_TOUCH_BEGIN and %GDK_TOUCH_END (or %GDK_TOUCH_CANCEL).
  5796 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_event_get_event_sequence() returns the event sequence for these
  5797 â”‚ â”‚            * events, so different sequences may be distinguished.
  5798 â”‚ â”‚            */
  5799 â”‚ â”‚   
  5800 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5801 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of bit-flags to indicate which events a window is to receive.
  5802 â”‚ â”‚            * Most of these masks map onto one or more of the #GdkEventType event types
  5803 â”‚ â”‚            * above.
  5804 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5805 â”‚ â”‚            * See the [input handling overview][chap-input-handling] for details of
  5806 â”‚ â”‚            * [event masks][event-masks] and [event propagation][event-propagation].
  5807 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5808 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_POINTER_MOTION_HINT_MASK is deprecated. It is a special mask
  5809 â”‚ â”‚            * to reduce the number of %GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY events received. When using
  5810 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_POINTER_MOTION_HINT_MASK, fewer %GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY events will
  5811 â”‚ â”‚            * be sent, some of which are marked as a hint (the is_hint member is
  5812 â”‚ â”‚            * %TRUE). To receive more motion events after a motion hint event,
  5813 â”‚ â”‚            * the application needs to asks for more, by calling
  5814 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_event_request_motions().
  5815 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5816 â”‚ â”‚            * Since GTK 3.8, motion events are already compressed by default, independent
  5817 â”‚ â”‚            * of this mechanism. This compression can be disabled with
  5818 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_window_set_event_compression(). See the documentation of that function
  5819 â”‚ â”‚            * for details.
  5820 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5821 â”‚ â”‚            * If %GDK_TOUCH_MASK is enabled, the window will receive touch events
  5822 â”‚ â”‚            * from touch-enabled devices. Those will come as sequences of #GdkEventTouch
  5823 â”‚ â”‚            * with type %GDK_TOUCH_UPDATE, enclosed by two events with
  5824 â”‚ â”‚            * type %GDK_TOUCH_BEGIN and %GDK_TOUCH_END (or %GDK_TOUCH_CANCEL).
  5825 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_event_get_event_sequence() returns the event sequence for these
  5826 â”‚ â”‚            * events, so different sequences may be distinguished.
  5827 â”‚ â”‚            */

  5988 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  5989 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of bit-flags to indicate the state of modifier keys and mouse buttons
  5990 â”‚ â”‚            * in various event types. Typical modifier keys are Shift, Control, Meta,
  5991 â”‚ â”‚            * Super, Hyper, Alt, Compose, Apple, CapsLock or ShiftLock.
  5992 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5993 â”‚ â”‚            * Like the X Window System, GDK supports 8 modifier keys and 5 mouse buttons.
  5994 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5995 â”‚ â”‚            * Since 2.10, GDK recognizes which of the Meta, Super or Hyper keys are mapped
  5996 â”‚ â”‚            * to Mod2 - Mod5, and indicates this by setting %GDK_SUPER_MASK,
  5997 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_HYPER_MASK or %GDK_META_MASK in the state field of key events.
  5998 â”‚ â”‚            *
  5999 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that GDK may add internal values to events which include
  6000 â”‚ â”‚            * reserved values such as %GDK_MODIFIER_RESERVED_13_MASK.  Your code
  6001 â”‚ â”‚            * should preserve and ignore them.  You can use %GDK_MODIFIER_MASK to
  6002 â”‚ â”‚            * remove all reserved values.
  6003 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6004 â”‚ â”‚            * Also note that the GDK X backend interprets button press events for button
  6005 â”‚ â”‚            * 4-7 as scroll events, so %GDK_BUTTON4_MASK and %GDK_BUTTON5_MASK will never
  6006 â”‚ â”‚            * be set.
  6007 â”‚ â”‚            */
  6008 â”‚ â”‚   
  6009 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  6010 â”‚ â”‚            * A set of bit-flags to indicate the state of modifier keys and mouse buttons
  6011 â”‚ â”‚            * in various event types. Typical modifier keys are Shift, Control, Meta,
  6012 â”‚ â”‚            * Super, Hyper, Alt, Compose, Apple, CapsLock or ShiftLock.
  6013 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6014 â”‚ â”‚            * Like the X Window System, GDK supports 8 modifier keys and 5 mouse buttons.

  6514 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  6515 â”‚ â”‚            * GdkAppLaunchContext is an implementation of #GAppLaunchContext that
  6516 â”‚ â”‚            * handles launching an application in a graphical context. It provides
  6517 â”‚ â”‚            * startup notification and allows to launch applications on a specific
  6518 â”‚ â”‚            * screen or workspace.
  6519 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6520 â”‚ â”‚            * ## Launching an application
  6521 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6522 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6523 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  6524 â”‚ â”‚            * GdkAppLaunchContext *context;
  6525 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6526 â”‚ â”‚            * context = gdk_display_get_app_launch_context (display);
  6527 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6528 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_app_launch_context_set_screen (screen);
  6529 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_app_launch_context_set_timestamp (event->time);
  6530 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6531 â”‚ â”‚            * if (!g_app_info_launch_default_for_uri ("http://www.gtk.org", context, &error))
  6532 â”‚ â”‚            *   g_warning ("Launching failed: %s\n", error->message);
  6533 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6534 â”‚ â”‚            * g_object_unref (context);
  6535 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  6536 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6537 â”‚ â”‚            */

  6586 â”‚ â”‚                * using this context when running under a window manager that
  6587 â”‚ â”‚                * supports multiple workspaces, as described in the

  6589 â”‚ â”‚                *

  6591 â”‚ â”‚                * it is up to the window manager to pick one, typically it will
  6592 â”‚ â”‚                * be the current workspace.

  6602 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  6604 â”‚ â”‚                * context.
  6605 â”‚ â”‚                *

  6607 â”‚ â”‚                * notification.

  6613 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  6614 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets the icon for applications that are launched with this context.
  6615 â”‚ â”‚                * The `icon_name` will be interpreted in the same way as the Icon field
  6616 â”‚ â”‚                * in desktop files. See also gdk_app_launch_context_set_icon().
  6617 â”‚ â”‚                *
  6618 â”‚ â”‚                * If both `icon` and `icon_name` are set, the `icon_name` takes priority.
  6619 â”‚ â”‚                * If neither `icon` or `icon_name` is set, the icon is taken from either
  6620 â”‚ â”‚                * the file that is passed to launched application or from the #GAppInfo
  6621 â”‚ â”‚                * for the launched application itself.
  6622 â”‚ â”‚                * @param icon_name an icon name, or %NULL
  6623 â”‚ â”‚                */

  6627 â”‚ â”‚                * using this context. See also gdk_app_launch_context_set_display().
  6628 â”‚ â”‚                *
  6629 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that, typically, a #GdkScreen represents a logical screen,
  6630 â”‚ â”‚                * not a physical monitor.
  6631 â”‚ â”‚                *
  6632 â”‚ â”‚                * If both `screen` and `display` are set, the `screen` takes priority.
  6633 â”‚ â”‚                * If neither `screen` or `display` are set, the default screen and
  6634 â”‚ â”‚                * display are used.
  6635 â”‚ â”‚                * @param screen a #GdkScreen
  6636 â”‚ â”‚                */
  6637 â”‚ â”‚               set_screen(screen: Screen): void;
  6638 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  6639 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets the timestamp of `context`. The timestamp should ideally
  6640 â”‚ â”‚                * be taken from the event that triggered the launch.
  6641 â”‚ â”‚                *
  6642 â”‚ â”‚                * Window managers can use this information to avoid moving the
  6643 â”‚ â”‚                * focus to the newly launched application when the user is busy
  6644 â”‚ â”‚                * typing in another window. This is also known as 'focus stealing
  6645 â”‚ â”‚                * prevention'.
  6646 â”‚ â”‚                * @param timestamp a timestamp
  6647 â”‚ â”‚                */
  6648 â”‚ â”‚               set_timestamp(timestamp: number): void;
  6649 â”‚ â”‚           }
  6650 â”‚ â”‚

  6816 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  6817 â”‚ â”‚            * The #GdkDevice object represents a single input device, such
  6818 â”‚ â”‚            * as a keyboard, a mouse, a touchpad, etc.
  6819 â”‚ â”‚            *
  6820 â”‚ â”‚            * See the #GdkDeviceManager documentation for more information

  6832 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7003 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a #GdkDisplay. This memory is owned          by GTK+, and must not be freed or unreffed.

  7005 â”‚ â”‚               get_display(): Display;
  7006 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7007 â”‚ â”‚                * Determines whether the pointer follows device motion.

  7012 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  7019 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  7080 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the vendor ID of this device, or %NULL if this information couldn't
  7081 â”‚ â”‚                * be obtained. This ID is retrieved from the device, and is thus constant for
  7082 â”‚ â”‚                * it.
  7083 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7084 â”‚ â”‚                * This function, together with gdk_device_get_product_id(), can be used to eg.
  7085 â”‚ â”‚                * compose #GSettings paths to store settings for this device.
  7086 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7087 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7088 â”‚ â”‚                * ```c
  7089 â”‚ â”‚                *  static GSettings *
  7090 â”‚ â”‚                *  get_device_settings (GdkDevice *device)
  7091 â”‚ â”‚                *  {

  7105 â”‚ â”‚                *  }

  7124 â”‚ â”‚                * belongs to another application).
  7125 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7126 â”‚ â”‚                * As a slave device coordinates are those of its master pointer, This
  7127 â”‚ â”‚                * function may not be called on devices of type %GDK_DEVICE_TYPE_SLAVE,
  7128 â”‚ â”‚                * unless there is an ongoing grab on them, see gdk_device_grab().
  7129 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the #GdkWindow under the   device position, or %NULL.
  7130 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7132 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7133 â”‚ â”‚                * Grabs the device so that all events coming from this device are passed to
  7134 â”‚ â”‚                * this application until the device is ungrabbed with gdk_device_ungrab(),
  7135 â”‚ â”‚                * or the window becomes unviewable. This overrides any previous grab on the device
  7136 â”‚ â”‚                * by this client.
  7137 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7138 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that `device` and `window` need to be on the same display.
  7139 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7140 â”‚ â”‚                * Device grabs are used for operations which need complete control over the
  7141 â”‚ â”‚                * given device events (either pointer or keyboard). For example in GTK+ this
  7142 â”‚ â”‚                * is used for Drag and Drop operations, popup menus and such.
  7143 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7144 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that if the event mask of an X window has selected both button press
  7145 â”‚ â”‚                * and button release events, then a button press event will cause an automatic
  7146 â”‚ â”‚                * pointer grab until the button is released. X does this automatically since
  7147 â”‚ â”‚                * most applications expect to receive button press and release events in pairs.
  7148 â”‚ â”‚                * It is equivalent to a pointer grab on the window with `owner_events` set to
  7149 â”‚ â”‚                * %TRUE.
  7150 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7151 â”‚ â”‚                * If you set up anything at the time you take the grab that needs to be
  7152 â”‚ â”‚                * cleaned up when the grab ends, you should handle the #GdkEventGrabBroken
  7153 â”‚ â”‚                * events that are emitted when the grab ends unvoluntarily.
  7154 â”‚ â”‚                * @param window the #GdkWindow which will own the grab (the grab window)
  7155 â”‚ â”‚                * @param grab_ownership specifies the grab ownership.
  7156 â”‚ â”‚                * @param owner_events if %FALSE then all device events are reported with respect to                @window and are only reported if selected by @event_mask. If                %TRUE then pointer events for this application are reported                as normal, but pointer events outside this application are                reported with respect to @window and only if selected by                @event_mask. In either mode, unreported events are discarded.
  7157 â”‚ â”‚                * @param event_mask specifies the event mask, which is used in accordance with              @owner_events.
  7158 â”‚ â”‚                * @param cursor the cursor to display while the grab is active if the device is          a pointer. If this is %NULL then the normal cursors are used for          @window and its descendants, and the cursor for @window is used          elsewhere.
  7159 â”‚ â”‚                * @param time_ the timestamp of the event which led to this pointer grab. This         usually comes from the #GdkEvent struct, though %GDK_CURRENT_TIME         can be used if the time isnâ€™t known.
  7160 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %GDK_GRAB_SUCCESS if the grab was successful.
  7161 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7162 â”‚ â”‚               grab(
  7163 â”‚ â”‚                   window: Window,
  7164 â”‚ â”‚                   grab_ownership: GrabOwnership | null,
  7165 â”‚ â”‚                   owner_events: boolean,
  7166 â”‚ â”‚                   event_mask: EventMask | null,
  7167 â”‚ â”‚                   cursor: Cursor | null,
  7168 â”‚ â”‚                   time_: number,
  7169 â”‚ â”‚               ): GrabStatus;
  7170 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7171 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns a #GList of #GdkAtoms, containing the labels for
  7172 â”‚ â”‚                * the axes that `device` currently has.
  7173 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns A #GList of #GdkAtoms, free with g_list_free().
  7174 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7175 â”‚ â”‚               list_axes(): Atom[];
  7176 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7177 â”‚ â”‚                * If the device if of type %GDK_DEVICE_TYPE_MASTER, it will return
