  7179 â”‚ â”‚                * %NULL
  7180 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the list of slave devices, or %NULL. The list must be          freed with g_list_free(), the contents of the list are          owned by GTK+ and should not be freed.
  7181 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7182 â”‚ â”‚               list_slave_devices(): Device[] | null;
  7183 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7184 â”‚ â”‚                * Specifies how an axis of a device is used.

  7188 â”‚ â”‚               set_axis_use(index_: number, use: AxisUse | null): void;
  7189 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7190 â”‚ â”‚                * Specifies the X key event to generate when a macro button of a device
  7191 â”‚ â”‚                * is pressed.
  7192 â”‚ â”‚                * @param index_ the index of the macro button to set

  7196 â”‚ â”‚               set_key(index_: number, keyval: number, modifiers: ModifierType | null): void;
  7197 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7198 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets a the mode of an input device. The mode controls if the
  7199 â”‚ â”‚                * device is active and whether the deviceâ€™s range is mapped to the
  7200 â”‚ â”‚                * entire screen or to a single window.
  7201 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7202 â”‚ â”‚                * Note: This is only meaningful for floating devices, master devices (and
  7203 â”‚ â”‚                * slaves connected to these) drive the pointer cursor, which is not limited
  7204 â”‚ â”‚                * by the input mode.

  7207 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7208 â”‚ â”‚               set_mode(mode: InputMode | null): boolean;
  7209 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7210 â”‚ â”‚                * Release any grab on `device`.
  7211 â”‚ â”‚                * @param time_ a timestap (e.g. %GDK_CURRENT_TIME).
  7212 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7213 â”‚ â”‚               ungrab(time_: number): void;
  7214 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7215 â”‚ â”‚                * Warps `device` in `display` to the point `x,``y` on
  7216 â”‚ â”‚                * the screen `screen,` unless the device is confined
  7217 â”‚ â”‚                * to a window by a grab, in which case it will be moved
  7218 â”‚ â”‚                * as far as allowed by the grab. Warping the pointer
  7219 â”‚ â”‚                * creates events as if the user had moved the mouse
  7220 â”‚ â”‚                * instantaneously to the destination.
  7221 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7222 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that the pointer should normally be under the
  7223 â”‚ â”‚                * control of the user. This function was added to cover
  7224 â”‚ â”‚                * some rare use cases like keyboard navigation support
  7225 â”‚ â”‚                * for the color picker in the #GtkColorSelectionDialog.
  7226 â”‚ â”‚                * @param screen the screen to warp @device to.
  7227 â”‚ â”‚                * @param x the X coordinate of the destination.
  7228 â”‚ â”‚                * @param y the Y coordinate of the destination.
  7229 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7230 â”‚ â”‚               warp(screen: Screen, x: number, y: number): void;
  7231 â”‚ â”‚           }
  7232 â”‚ â”‚   
  7233 â”‚ â”‚           namespace DeviceManager {
  7234 â”‚ â”‚               // Signal signatures
  7235 â”‚ â”‚               interface SignalSignatures extends GObject.Object.SignalSignatures {
  7236 â”‚ â”‚                   'device-added': (arg0: Device) => void;
  7237 â”‚ â”‚                   'device-changed': (arg0: Device) => void;
  7238 â”‚ â”‚                   'device-removed': (arg0: Device) => void;
  7239 â”‚ â”‚                   'notify::display': (pspec: GObject.ParamSpec) => void;
  7240 â”‚ â”‚               }
  7241 â”‚ â”‚   
  7242 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructor properties interface
  7243 â”‚ â”‚   
  7244 â”‚ â”‚               interface ConstructorProps extends GObject.Object.ConstructorProps {
  7245 â”‚ â”‚                   display: Display;
  7246 â”‚ â”‚               }
  7247 â”‚ â”‚           }
  7248 â”‚ â”‚   
  7249 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  7250 â”‚ â”‚            * In addition to a single pointer and keyboard for user interface input,
  7251 â”‚ â”‚            * GDK contains support for a variety of input devices, including graphics
  7252 â”‚ â”‚            * tablets, touchscreens and multiple pointers/keyboards interacting
  7253 â”‚ â”‚            * simultaneously with the user interface. Such input devices often have
  7254 â”‚ â”‚            * additional features, such as sub-pixel positioning information and
  7255 â”‚ â”‚            * additional device-dependent information.
  7256 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7257 â”‚ â”‚            * In order to query the device hierarchy and be aware of changes in the
  7258 â”‚ â”‚            * device hierarchy (such as virtual devices being created or removed, or
  7259 â”‚ â”‚            * physical devices being plugged or unplugged), GDK provides
  7260 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkDeviceManager.
  7261 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7262 â”‚ â”‚            * By default, and if the platform supports it, GDK is aware of multiple
  7263 â”‚ â”‚            * keyboard/pointer pairs and multitouch devices. This behavior can be
  7264 â”‚ â”‚            * changed by calling gdk_disable_multidevice() before gdk_display_open().
  7265 â”‚ â”‚            * There should rarely be a need to do that though, since GDK defaults
  7266 â”‚ â”‚            * to a compatibility mode in which it will emit just one enter/leave
  7267 â”‚ â”‚            * event pair for all devices on a window. To enable per-device
  7268 â”‚ â”‚            * enter/leave events and other multi-pointer interaction features,
  7269 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_window_set_support_multidevice() must be called on
  7270 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkWindows (or gtk_widget_set_support_multidevice() on widgets).
  7271 â”‚ â”‚            * window. See the gdk_window_set_support_multidevice() documentation
  7272 â”‚ â”‚            * for more information.
  7273 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7274 â”‚ â”‚            * On X11, multi-device support is implemented through XInput 2.
  7275 â”‚ â”‚            * Unless gdk_disable_multidevice() is called, the XInput 2
  7276 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkDeviceManager implementation will be used as the input source.
  7277 â”‚ â”‚            * Otherwise either the core or XInput 1 implementations will be used.
  7278 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7279 â”‚ â”‚            * For simple applications that donâ€™t have any special interest in
  7280 â”‚ â”‚            * input devices, the so-called â€œclient pointerâ€
  7281 â”‚ â”‚            * provides a reasonable approximation to a simple setup with a single
  7282 â”‚ â”‚            * pointer and keyboard. The device that has been set as the client
  7283 â”‚ â”‚            * pointer can be accessed via gdk_device_manager_get_client_pointer().
  7284 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7285 â”‚ â”‚            * Conceptually, in multidevice mode there are 2 device types. Virtual
  7286 â”‚ â”‚            * devices (or master devices) are represented by the pointer cursors
  7287 â”‚ â”‚            * and keyboard foci that are seen on the screen. Physical devices (or
  7288 â”‚ â”‚            * slave devices) represent the hardware that is controlling the virtual
  7289 â”‚ â”‚            * devices, and thus have no visible cursor on the screen.
  7290 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7291 â”‚ â”‚            * Virtual devices are always paired, so there is a keyboard device for every
  7292 â”‚ â”‚            * pointer device. Associations between devices may be inspected through
  7293 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_device_get_associated_device().
  7294 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7295 â”‚ â”‚            * There may be several virtual devices, and several physical devices could
  7296 â”‚ â”‚            * be controlling each of these virtual devices. Physical devices may also
  7297 â”‚ â”‚            * be â€œfloatingâ€, which means they are not attached to any virtual device.
  7298 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7299 â”‚ â”‚            * # Master and slave devices
  7300 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7301 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7302 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  7303 â”‚ â”‚            * carlos`sacarino:`~$ xinput list
  7304 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽ¡ Virtual core pointer                          id=2    [master pointer  (3)]
  7305 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ Virtual core XTEST pointer                id=4    [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7306 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ Wacom ISDv4 E6 Pen stylus                 id=10   [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7307 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ Wacom ISDv4 E6 Finger touch               id=11   [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7308 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ SynPS/2 Synaptics TouchPad                id=13   [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7309 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ TPPS/2 IBM TrackPoint                     id=14   [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7310 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽœ   â†³ Wacom ISDv4 E6 Pen eraser                 id=16   [slave  pointer  (2)]
  7311 â”‚ â”‚            * âŽ£ Virtual core keyboard                         id=3    [master keyboard (2)]
  7312 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ Virtual core XTEST keyboard               id=5    [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7313 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ Power Button                              id=6    [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7314 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ Video Bus                                 id=7    [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7315 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ Sleep Button                              id=8    [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7316 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ Integrated Camera                         id=9    [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7317 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ AT Translated Set 2 keyboard              id=12   [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7318 â”‚ â”‚            *     â†³ ThinkPad Extra Buttons                    id=15   [slave  keyboard (3)]
  7319 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  7320 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7321 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7322 â”‚ â”‚            * By default, GDK will automatically listen for events coming from all
  7323 â”‚ â”‚            * master devices, setting the #GdkDevice for all events coming from input
  7324 â”‚ â”‚            * devices. Events containing device information are #GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY,
  7325 â”‚ â”‚            * #GDK_BUTTON_PRESS, #GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS, #GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS,
  7326 â”‚ â”‚            * #GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE, #GDK_SCROLL, #GDK_KEY_PRESS, #GDK_KEY_RELEASE,
  7327 â”‚ â”‚            * #GDK_ENTER_NOTIFY, #GDK_LEAVE_NOTIFY, #GDK_FOCUS_CHANGE,
  7328 â”‚ â”‚            * #GDK_PROXIMITY_IN, #GDK_PROXIMITY_OUT, #GDK_DRAG_ENTER, #GDK_DRAG_LEAVE,
  7329 â”‚ â”‚            * #GDK_DRAG_MOTION, #GDK_DRAG_STATUS, #GDK_DROP_START, #GDK_DROP_FINISHED
  7330 â”‚ â”‚            * and #GDK_GRAB_BROKEN. When dealing with an event on a master device,
  7331 â”‚ â”‚            * it is possible to get the source (slave) device that the event originated
  7332 â”‚ â”‚            * from via gdk_event_get_source_device().
  7333 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7334 â”‚ â”‚            * On a standard session, all physical devices are connected by default to
  7335 â”‚ â”‚            * the "Virtual Core Pointer/Keyboard" master devices, hence routing all events
  7336 â”‚ â”‚            * through these. This behavior is only modified by device grabs, where the
  7337 â”‚ â”‚            * slave device is temporarily detached for as long as the grab is held, and
  7338 â”‚ â”‚            * more permanently by user modifications to the device hierarchy.
  7339 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7340 â”‚ â”‚            * On certain application specific setups, it may make sense
  7341 â”‚ â”‚            * to detach a physical device from its master pointer, and mapping it to
  7342 â”‚ â”‚            * an specific window. This can be achieved by the combination of
  7343 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_device_grab() and gdk_device_set_mode().
  7344 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7345 â”‚ â”‚            * In order to listen for events coming from devices
  7346 â”‚ â”‚            * other than a virtual device, gdk_window_set_device_events() must be
  7347 â”‚ â”‚            * called. Generally, this function can be used to modify the event mask
  7348 â”‚ â”‚            * for any given device.
  7349 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7350 â”‚ â”‚            * Input devices may also provide additional information besides X/Y.
  7351 â”‚ â”‚            * For example, graphics tablets may also provide pressure and X/Y tilt
  7352 â”‚ â”‚            * information. This information is device-dependent, and may be
  7353 â”‚ â”‚            * queried through gdk_device_get_axis(). In multidevice mode, virtual
  7354 â”‚ â”‚            * devices will change axes in order to always represent the physical
  7355 â”‚ â”‚            * device that is routing events through it. Whenever the physical device
  7356 â”‚ â”‚            * changes, the #GdkDevice:n-axes property will be notified, and
  7357 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_device_list_axes() will return the new device axes.
  7358 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7359 â”‚ â”‚            * Devices may also have associated â€œkeysâ€ or
  7360 â”‚ â”‚            * macro buttons. Such keys can be globally set to map into normal X
  7361 â”‚ â”‚            * keyboard events. The mapping is set using gdk_device_set_key().
  7362 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7363 â”‚ â”‚            * In GTK+ 3.20, a new #GdkSeat object has been introduced that
  7364 â”‚ â”‚            * supersedes #GdkDeviceManager and should be preferred in newly
  7365 â”‚ â”‚            * written code.
  7366 â”‚ â”‚            */
  7367 â”‚ â”‚           abstract class DeviceManager extends GObject.Object {

  7412 â”‚ â”‚                * pattern under the presence of several pointers.

  7429 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7542 â”‚ â”‚   
  7543 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  7544 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkDisplay objects purpose are two fold:
  7545 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7546 â”‚ â”‚            * - To manage and provide information about input devices (pointers and keyboards)
  7547 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7548 â”‚ â”‚            * - To manage and provide information about the available #GdkScreens
  7549 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7550 â”‚ â”‚            * GdkDisplay objects are the GDK representation of an X Display,
  7551 â”‚ â”‚            * which can be described as a workstation consisting of
  7552 â”‚ â”‚            * a keyboard, a pointing device (such as a mouse) and one or more
  7553 â”‚ â”‚            * screens.
  7554 â”‚ â”‚            * It is used to open and keep track of various GdkScreen objects
  7555 â”‚ â”‚            * currently instantiated by the application. It is also used to
  7556 â”‚ â”‚            * access the keyboard(s) and mouse pointer(s) of the display.
  7557 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7558 â”‚ â”‚            * Most of the input device handling has been factored out into
  7559 â”‚ â”‚            * the separate #GdkDeviceManager object. Every display has a
  7560 â”‚ â”‚            * device manager, which you can obtain using
  7561 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_display_get_device_manager().
  7562 â”‚ â”‚            */

  7634 â”‚ â”‚                * @param device a #GdkDevice

  7636 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7638 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7639 â”‚ â”‚                * Flushes any requests queued for the windowing system; this happens automatically
  7640 â”‚ â”‚                * when the main loop blocks waiting for new events, but if your application
  7641 â”‚ â”‚                * is drawing without returning control to the main loop, you may need
  7642 â”‚ â”‚                * to call this function explicitly. A common case where this function
  7643 â”‚ â”‚                * needs to be called is when an application is executing drawing commands
  7644 â”‚ â”‚                * from a thread other than the thread where the main loop is running.
  7645 â”‚ â”‚                *
  7646 â”‚ â”‚                * This is most useful for X11. On windowing systems where requests are
  7647 â”‚ â”‚                * handled synchronously, this function will do nothing.
  7648 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7650 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  7656 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7657 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the default size to use for cursors on `display`.

  7661 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7662 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the default group leader window for all toplevel windows

  7664 â”‚ â”‚                * See gdk_window_set_group().

  7666 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7668 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7669 â”‚ â”‚                * Get the default #GdkScreen for `display`.

  7671 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7672 â”‚ â”‚               get_default_screen(): Screen;
  7673 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  7674 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the default #GdkSeat for this display.
  7675 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the default seat.
  7676 â”‚ â”‚                */
  7677 â”‚ â”‚               get_default_seat(): Seat;

  7909 â”‚ â”‚                * requests have been handled. This is often used for making sure that the
  7910 â”‚ â”‚                * display is synchronized with the current state of the program. Calling
  7911 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_display_sync() before gdk_error_trap_pop() makes sure that any errors
  7912 â”‚ â”‚                * generated from earlier requests are handled before the error trap is

  7916 â”‚ â”‚                * handled synchronously, this function will do nothing.

  7921 â”‚ â”‚                * the screen `screen,` unless the pointer is confined
  7922 â”‚ â”‚                * to a window by a grab, in which case it will be moved
  7923 â”‚ â”‚                * as far as allowed by the grab. Warping the pointer
  7924 â”‚ â”‚                * creates events as if the user had moved the mouse
  7925 â”‚ â”‚                * instantaneously to the destination.
  7926 â”‚ â”‚                *

  7928 â”‚ â”‚                * control of the user. This function was added to cover
  7929 â”‚ â”‚                * some rare use cases like keyboard navigation support
  7930 â”‚ â”‚                * for the color picker in the #GtkColorSelectionDialog.
  7931 â”‚ â”‚                * @param screen the screen of @display to warp the pointer to
  7932 â”‚ â”‚                * @param x the x coordinate of the destination
  7933 â”‚ â”‚                * @param y the y coordinate of the destination
  7934 â”‚ â”‚                */

  7938 â”‚ â”‚           namespace DisplayManager {
  7939 â”‚ â”‚               // Signal signatures
  7940 â”‚ â”‚               interface SignalSignatures extends GObject.Object.SignalSignatures {
  7941 â”‚ â”‚                   'display-opened': (arg0: Display) => void;
  7942 â”‚ â”‚                   'notify::default-display': (pspec: GObject.ParamSpec) => void;
  7943 â”‚ â”‚               }
  7944 â”‚ â”‚   
  7945 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructor properties interface
  7946 â”‚ â”‚   
  7947 â”‚ â”‚               interface ConstructorProps extends GObject.Object.ConstructorProps {
  7948 â”‚ â”‚                   default_display: Display;
  7949 â”‚ â”‚                   defaultDisplay: Display;
  7950 â”‚ â”‚               }
  7951 â”‚ â”‚           }
  7952 â”‚ â”‚   
  7953 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  7954 â”‚ â”‚            * The purpose of the #GdkDisplayManager singleton object is to offer
  7955 â”‚ â”‚            * notification when displays appear or disappear or the default display
  7956 â”‚ â”‚            * changes.
  7957 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7958 â”‚ â”‚            * You can use gdk_display_manager_get() to obtain the #GdkDisplayManager
  7959 â”‚ â”‚            * singleton, but that should be rarely necessary. Typically, initializing
  7960 â”‚ â”‚            * GTK+ opens a display that you can work with without ever accessing the
  7961 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkDisplayManager.
  7962 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7963 â”‚ â”‚            * The GDK library can be built with support for multiple backends.
  7964 â”‚ â”‚            * The #GdkDisplayManager object determines which backend is used
  7965 â”‚ â”‚            * at runtime.
  7966 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7967 â”‚ â”‚            * When writing backend-specific code that is supposed to work with
  7968 â”‚ â”‚            * multiple GDK backends, you have to consider both compile time and
  7969 â”‚ â”‚            * runtime. At compile time, use the #GDK_WINDOWING_X11, #GDK_WINDOWING_WIN32
  7970 â”‚ â”‚            * macros, etc. to find out which backends are present in the GDK library
  7971 â”‚ â”‚            * you are building your application against. At runtime, use type-check
  7972 â”‚ â”‚            * macros like GDK_IS_X11_DISPLAY() to find out which backend is in use:
  7973 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7974 â”‚ â”‚            * ## Backend-specific code ## {#backend-specific}
  7975 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7976 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7977 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  7978 â”‚ â”‚            * #ifdef GDK_WINDOWING_X11
  7979 â”‚ â”‚            *   if (GDK_IS_X11_DISPLAY (display))
  7980 â”‚ â”‚            *     {
  7981 â”‚ â”‚            *       // make X11-specific calls here
  7982 â”‚ â”‚            *     }
  7983 â”‚ â”‚            *   else
  7984 â”‚ â”‚            * #endif
  7985 â”‚ â”‚            * #ifdef GDK_WINDOWING_QUARTZ
  7986 â”‚ â”‚            *   if (GDK_IS_QUARTZ_DISPLAY (display))
  7987 â”‚ â”‚            *     {
  7988 â”‚ â”‚            *       // make Quartz-specific calls here
  7989 â”‚ â”‚            *     }
  7990 â”‚ â”‚            *   else
  7991 â”‚ â”‚            * #endif
  7992 â”‚ â”‚            *   g_error ("Unsupported GDK backend");
  7993 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  7994 â”‚ â”‚            *
  7995 â”‚ â”‚            */
  7996 â”‚ â”‚           class DisplayManager extends GObject.Object {
  7997 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<DisplayManager>;
  7998 â”‚ â”‚   
  7999 â”‚ â”‚               // Properties
  8000 â”‚ â”‚   
  8001 â”‚ â”‚               get default_display(): Display;
  8002 â”‚ â”‚               set default_display(val: Display);
  8003 â”‚ â”‚               get defaultDisplay(): Display;
  8004 â”‚ â”‚               set defaultDisplay(val: Display);
  8005 â”‚ â”‚   
  8006 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8007 â”‚ â”‚                * Compile-time signal type information.
  8008 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8009 â”‚ â”‚                * This instance property is generated only for TypeScript type checking.
  8010 â”‚ â”‚                * It is not defined at runtime and should not be accessed in JS code.
  8011 â”‚ â”‚                * @internal
  8012 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8013 â”‚ â”‚               $signals: DisplayManager.SignalSignatures;
  8014 â”‚ â”‚   
  8015 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructors
  8016 â”‚ â”‚   
  8017 â”‚ â”‚               constructor(properties?: Partial<DisplayManager.ConstructorProps>, ...args: any[]);
  8018 â”‚ â”‚   
  8019 â”‚ â”‚               _init(...args: any[]): void;
  8020 â”‚ â”‚   
  8021 â”‚ â”‚               // Signals
  8022 â”‚ â”‚   
  8023 â”‚ â”‚               connect<K extends keyof DisplayManager.SignalSignatures>(
  8024 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,
  8025 â”‚ â”‚                   callback: GObject.SignalCallback<this, DisplayManager.SignalSignatures[K]>,
  8026 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  8027 â”‚ â”‚               connect(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;
  8028 â”‚ â”‚               connect_after<K extends keyof DisplayManager.SignalSignatures>(
  8029 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,
  8030 â”‚ â”‚                   callback: GObject.SignalCallback<this, DisplayManager.SignalSignatures[K]>,
  8031 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  8032 â”‚ â”‚               connect_after(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;

  8181 â”‚ â”‚                * Requests the drag and drop operation to be managed by `context`.
  8182 â”‚ â”‚                * When a drag and drop operation becomes managed, the #GdkDragContext
  8183 â”‚ â”‚                * will internally handle all input and source-side #GdkEventDND events
  8184 â”‚ â”‚                * as required by the windowing system.

  8200 â”‚ â”‚                */

  8321 â”‚ â”‚           namespace FrameClock {
  8322 â”‚ â”‚               // Signal signatures
  8323 â”‚ â”‚               interface SignalSignatures extends GObject.Object.SignalSignatures {
  8324 â”‚ â”‚                   'after-paint': () => void;
  8325 â”‚ â”‚                   'before-paint': () => void;
  8326 â”‚ â”‚                   'flush-events': () => void;
  8327 â”‚ â”‚                   layout: () => void;
  8328 â”‚ â”‚                   paint: () => void;
  8329 â”‚ â”‚                   'resume-events': () => void;
  8330 â”‚ â”‚                   update: () => void;
  8331 â”‚ â”‚               }
  8332 â”‚ â”‚   
  8333 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructor properties interface
  8334 â”‚ â”‚   
  8335 â”‚ â”‚               interface ConstructorProps extends GObject.Object.ConstructorProps {}
  8336 â”‚ â”‚           }
  8337 â”‚ â”‚   
  8338 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  8339 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkFrameClock tells the application when to update and repaint a
  8340 â”‚ â”‚            * window. This may be synced to the vertical refresh rate of the
  8341 â”‚ â”‚            * monitor, for example. Even when the frame clock uses a simple timer
  8342 â”‚ â”‚            * rather than a hardware-based vertical sync, the frame clock helps
  8343 â”‚ â”‚            * because it ensures everything paints at the same time (reducing the
  8344 â”‚ â”‚            * total number of frames). The frame clock can also automatically
  8345 â”‚ â”‚            * stop painting when it knows the frames will not be visible, or
  8346 â”‚ â”‚            * scale back animation framerates.
  8347 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8348 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkFrameClock is designed to be compatible with an OpenGL-based
  8349 â”‚ â”‚            * implementation or with mozRequestAnimationFrame in Firefox,
  8350 â”‚ â”‚            * for example.
  8351 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8352 â”‚ â”‚            * A frame clock is idle until someone requests a frame with
  8353 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_frame_clock_request_phase(). At some later point that makes
  8354 â”‚ â”‚            * sense for the synchronization being implemented, the clock will
  8355 â”‚ â”‚            * process a frame and emit signals for each phase that has been
  8356 â”‚ â”‚            * requested. (See the signals of the #GdkFrameClock class for
  8357 â”‚ â”‚            * documentation of the phases. %GDK_FRAME_CLOCK_PHASE_UPDATE and the
  8358 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkFrameClock::update signal are most interesting for application
  8359 â”‚ â”‚            * writers, and are used to update the animations, using the frame time
  8360 â”‚ â”‚            * given by gdk_frame_clock_get_frame_time().
  8361 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8362 â”‚ â”‚            * The frame time is reported in microseconds and generally in the same
  8363 â”‚ â”‚            * timescale as g_get_monotonic_time(), however, it is not the same
  8364 â”‚ â”‚            * as g_get_monotonic_time(). The frame time does not advance during
  8365 â”‚ â”‚            * the time a frame is being painted, and outside of a frame, an attempt
  8366 â”‚ â”‚            * is made so that all calls to gdk_frame_clock_get_frame_time() that
  8367 â”‚ â”‚            * are called at a â€œsimilarâ€ time get the same value. This means that
  8368 â”‚ â”‚            * if different animations are timed by looking at the difference in
  8369 â”‚ â”‚            * time between an initial value from gdk_frame_clock_get_frame_time()
  8370 â”‚ â”‚            * and the value inside the #GdkFrameClock::update signal of the clock,
  8371 â”‚ â”‚            * they will stay exactly synchronized.
  8372 â”‚ â”‚            */
  8373 â”‚ â”‚           abstract class FrameClock extends GObject.Object {
  8374 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<FrameClock>;
  8375 â”‚ â”‚   
  8376 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8377 â”‚ â”‚                * Compile-time signal type information.
  8378 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8379 â”‚ â”‚                * This instance property is generated only for TypeScript type checking.
  8380 â”‚ â”‚                * It is not defined at runtime and should not be accessed in JS code.
  8381 â”‚ â”‚                * @internal
  8382 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8383 â”‚ â”‚               $signals: FrameClock.SignalSignatures;
  8384 â”‚ â”‚   
  8385 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructors
  8386 â”‚ â”‚   
  8387 â”‚ â”‚               constructor(properties?: Partial<FrameClock.ConstructorProps>, ...args: any[]);
  8388 â”‚ â”‚   
  8389 â”‚ â”‚               _init(...args: any[]): void;
  8390 â”‚ â”‚   
  8391 â”‚ â”‚               // Signals
  8392 â”‚ â”‚   
  8393 â”‚ â”‚               connect<K extends keyof FrameClock.SignalSignatures>(
  8394 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,
  8395 â”‚ â”‚                   callback: GObject.SignalCallback<this, FrameClock.SignalSignatures[K]>,
  8396 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  8397 â”‚ â”‚               connect(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;
  8398 â”‚ â”‚               connect_after<K extends keyof FrameClock.SignalSignatures>(
  8399 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,
  8400 â”‚ â”‚                   callback: GObject.SignalCallback<this, FrameClock.SignalSignatures[K]>,
  8401 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  8402 â”‚ â”‚               connect_after(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;
  8403 â”‚ â”‚               emit<K extends keyof FrameClock.SignalSignatures>(
  8404 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,
  8405 â”‚ â”‚                   ...args: GObject.GjsParameters<FrameClock.SignalSignatures[K]> extends [any, ...infer Q] ? Q : never
  8406 â”‚ â”‚               ): void;
  8407 â”‚ â”‚               emit(signal: string, ...args: any[]): void;
  8408 â”‚ â”‚   
  8409 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
  8410 â”‚ â”‚   
  8411 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8412 â”‚ â”‚                * Starts updates for an animation. Until a matching call to
  8413 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_end_updating() is made, the frame clock will continually
  8414 â”‚ â”‚                * request a new frame with the %GDK_FRAME_CLOCK_PHASE_UPDATE phase.
  8415 â”‚ â”‚                * This function may be called multiple times and frames will be
  8416 â”‚ â”‚                * requested until gdk_frame_clock_end_updating() is called the same
  8417 â”‚ â”‚                * number of times.
  8418 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8419 â”‚ â”‚               begin_updating(): void;
  8420 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8421 â”‚ â”‚                * Stops updates for an animation. See the documentation for
  8422 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_begin_updating().
  8423 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8424 â”‚ â”‚               end_updating(): void;
  8425 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8426 â”‚ â”‚                * Gets the frame timings for the current frame.
  8427 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the #GdkFrameTimings for the  frame currently being processed, or even no frame is being  processed, for the previous frame. Before any frames have been  processed, returns %NULL.
  8428 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8429 â”‚ â”‚               get_current_timings(): FrameTimings | null;
  8430 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8431 â”‚ â”‚                * A #GdkFrameClock maintains a 64-bit counter that increments for
  8432 â”‚ â”‚                * each frame drawn.
  8433 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns inside frame processing, the value of the frame counter  for the current frame. Outside of frame processing, the frame   counter for the last frame.
  8434 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8435 â”‚ â”‚               get_frame_counter(): number;
  8436 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8437 â”‚ â”‚                * Gets the time that should currently be used for animations.  Inside
  8438 â”‚ â”‚                * the processing of a frame, itâ€™s the time used to compute the
  8439 â”‚ â”‚                * animation position of everything in a frame. Outside of a frame, it's
  8440 â”‚ â”‚                * the time of the conceptual â€œprevious frame,â€ which may be either
  8441 â”‚ â”‚                * the actual previous frame time, or if thatâ€™s too old, an updated
  8442 â”‚ â”‚                * time.
  8443 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a timestamp in microseconds, in the timescale of  of g_get_monotonic_time().
  8444 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8445 â”‚ â”‚               get_frame_time(): number;
  8446 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8447 â”‚ â”‚                * #GdkFrameClock internally keeps a history of #GdkFrameTimings
  8448 â”‚ â”‚                * objects for recent frames that can be retrieved with
  8449 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_get_timings(). The set of stored frames
  8450 â”‚ â”‚                * is the set from the counter values given by
  8451 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_get_history_start() and
  8452 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_get_frame_counter(), inclusive.
  8453 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the frame counter value for the oldest frame  that is available in the internal frame history of the  #GdkFrameClock.
  8454 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8455 â”‚ â”‚               get_history_start(): number;
  8456 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8457 â”‚ â”‚                * Using the frame history stored in the frame clock, finds the last
  8458 â”‚ â”‚                * known presentation time and refresh interval, and assuming that
  8459 â”‚ â”‚                * presentation times are separated by the refresh interval,
  8460 â”‚ â”‚                * predicts a presentation time that is a multiple of the refresh
  8461 â”‚ â”‚                * interval after the last presentation time, and later than `base_time`.
  8462 â”‚ â”‚                * @param base_time base time for determining a presentaton time
  8463 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8464 â”‚ â”‚               get_refresh_info(base_time: number): [number, number];
  8465 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8466 â”‚ â”‚                * Retrieves a #GdkFrameTimings object holding timing information
  8467 â”‚ â”‚                * for the current frame or a recent frame. The #GdkFrameTimings
  8468 â”‚ â”‚                * object may not yet be complete: see gdk_frame_timings_get_complete().
  8469 â”‚ â”‚                * @param frame_counter the frame counter value identifying the frame to  be received.
  8470 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the #GdkFrameTimings object for  the specified frame, or %NULL if it is not available. See  gdk_frame_clock_get_history_start().
  8471 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8472 â”‚ â”‚               get_timings(frame_counter: number): FrameTimings | null;
  8473 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8474 â”‚ â”‚                * Asks the frame clock to run a particular phase. The signal
  8475 â”‚ â”‚                * corresponding the requested phase will be emitted the next
  8476 â”‚ â”‚                * time the frame clock processes. Multiple calls to
  8477 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_clock_request_phase() will be combined together
  8478 â”‚ â”‚                * and only one frame processed. If you are displaying animated
  8479 â”‚ â”‚                * content and want to continually request the
  8480 â”‚ â”‚                * %GDK_FRAME_CLOCK_PHASE_UPDATE phase for a period of time,
  8481 â”‚ â”‚                * you should use gdk_frame_clock_begin_updating() instead, since
  8482 â”‚ â”‚                * this allows GTK+ to adjust system parameters to get maximally
  8483 â”‚ â”‚                * smooth animations.
  8484 â”‚ â”‚                * @param phase the phase that is requested
  8485 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8486 â”‚ â”‚               request_phase(phase: FrameClockPhase | null): void;
  8487 â”‚ â”‚           }
  8488 â”‚ â”‚   
  8489 â”‚ â”‚           namespace GLContext {
  8490 â”‚ â”‚               // Signal signatures
  8491 â”‚ â”‚               interface SignalSignatures extends GObject.Object.SignalSignatures {
  8492 â”‚ â”‚                   'notify::display': (pspec: GObject.ParamSpec) => void;
  8493 â”‚ â”‚                   'notify::shared-context': (pspec: GObject.ParamSpec) => void;
  8494 â”‚ â”‚                   'notify::window': (pspec: GObject.ParamSpec) => void;
  8495 â”‚ â”‚               }
  8496 â”‚ â”‚   
  8497 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructor properties interface
  8498 â”‚ â”‚   
  8499 â”‚ â”‚               interface ConstructorProps extends GObject.Object.ConstructorProps {
  8500 â”‚ â”‚                   display: Display;
  8501 â”‚ â”‚                   shared_context: GLContext;
  8502 â”‚ â”‚                   sharedContext: GLContext;
  8503 â”‚ â”‚                   window: Window;
  8504 â”‚ â”‚               }
  8505 â”‚ â”‚           }
  8506 â”‚ â”‚   
  8507 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  8508 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkGLContext is an object representing the platform-specific
  8509 â”‚ â”‚            * OpenGL drawing context.
  8510 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8511 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkGLContexts are created for a #GdkWindow using
  8512 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_window_create_gl_context(), and the context will match
  8513 â”‚ â”‚            * the #GdkVisual of the window.
  8514 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8515 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkGLContext is not tied to any particular normal framebuffer.
  8516 â”‚ â”‚            * For instance, it cannot draw to the #GdkWindow back buffer. The GDK
  8517 â”‚ â”‚            * repaint system is in full control of the painting to that. Instead,
  8518 â”‚ â”‚            * you can create render buffers or textures and use gdk_cairo_draw_from_gl()
  8519 â”‚ â”‚            * in the draw function of your widget to draw them. Then GDK will handle
  8520 â”‚ â”‚            * the integration of your rendering with that of other widgets.
  8521 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8522 â”‚ â”‚            * Support for #GdkGLContext is platform-specific, context creation
  8523 â”‚ â”‚            * can fail, returning %NULL context.
  8524 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8525 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkGLContext has to be made "current" in order to start using
  8526 â”‚ â”‚            * it, otherwise any OpenGL call will be ignored.
  8527 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8528 â”‚ â”‚            * ## Creating a new OpenGL context ##
  8529 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8530 â”‚ â”‚            * In order to create a new #GdkGLContext instance you need a
  8531 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkWindow, which you typically get during the realize call
  8532 â”‚ â”‚            * of a widget.
  8533 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8534 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkGLContext is not realized until either gdk_gl_context_make_current(),
  8535 â”‚ â”‚            * or until it is realized using gdk_gl_context_realize(). It is possible to
  8536 â”‚ â”‚            * specify details of the GL context like the OpenGL version to be used, or
  8537 â”‚ â”‚            * whether the GL context should have extra state validation enabled after
  8538 â”‚ â”‚            * calling gdk_window_create_gl_context() by calling gdk_gl_context_realize().
  8539 â”‚ â”‚            * If the realization fails you have the option to change the settings of the
  8540 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkGLContext and try again.
  8541 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8542 â”‚ â”‚            * ## Using a GdkGLContext ##
  8543 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8544 â”‚ â”‚            * You will need to make the #GdkGLContext the current context
  8545 â”‚ â”‚            * before issuing OpenGL calls; the system sends OpenGL commands to
  8546 â”‚ â”‚            * whichever context is current. It is possible to have multiple
  8547 â”‚ â”‚            * contexts, so you always need to ensure that the one which you
  8548 â”‚ â”‚            * want to draw with is the current one before issuing commands:
  8549 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8550 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8551 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
  8552 â”‚ â”‚            *   gdk_gl_context_make_current (context);
  8553 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
  8554 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8555 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8556 â”‚ â”‚            * You can now perform your drawing using OpenGL commands.
  8557 â”‚ â”‚            *
  8558 â”‚ â”‚            * You can check which #GdkGLContext is the current one by using
  8559 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_gl_context_get_current(); you can also unset any #GdkGLContext
  8560 â”‚ â”‚            * that is currently set by calling gdk_gl_context_clear_current().
  8561 â”‚ â”‚            */
  8562 â”‚ â”‚           abstract class GLContext extends GObject.Object {
  8563 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<GLContext>;
  8564 â”‚ â”‚   
  8565 â”‚ â”‚               // Properties
  8566 â”‚ â”‚   
  8567 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8568 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkDisplay used to create the #GdkGLContext.
  8569 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8570 â”‚ â”‚               get display(): Display;
  8571 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8572 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkGLContext that this context is sharing data with, or %NULL
  8573 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8574 â”‚ â”‚               get shared_context(): GLContext;
  8575 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  8582 â”‚ â”‚               get window(): Window;

  8670 â”‚ â”‚                * Retrieves the #GdkWindow used by the `context`.
  8671 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a #GdkWindow or %NULL
  8672 â”‚ â”‚                */

  8674 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8675 â”‚ â”‚                * Whether the #GdkGLContext is in legacy mode or not.
  8676 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8677 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkGLContext must be realized before calling this function.
  8678 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8679 â”‚ â”‚                * When realizing a GL context, GDK will try to use the OpenGL 3.2 core
  8680 â”‚ â”‚                * profile; this profile removes all the OpenGL API that was deprecated
  8681 â”‚ â”‚                * prior to the 3.2 version of the specification. If the realization is
  8682 â”‚ â”‚                * successful, this function will return %FALSE.
  8683 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8684 â”‚ â”‚                * If the underlying OpenGL implementation does not support core profiles,
  8685 â”‚ â”‚                * GDK will fall back to a pre-3.2 compatibility profile, and this function
  8686 â”‚ â”‚                * will return %TRUE.
  8687 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8688 â”‚ â”‚                * You can use the value returned by this function to decide which kind
  8689 â”‚ â”‚                * of OpenGL API to use, or whether to do extension discovery, or what
  8690 â”‚ â”‚                * kind of shader programs to load.
  8691 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the GL context is in legacy mode
  8692 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8693 â”‚ â”‚               is_legacy(): boolean;
  8694 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8695 â”‚ â”‚                * Makes the `context` the current one.
  8696 â”‚ â”‚                */

  8698 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8699 â”‚ â”‚                * Realizes the given #GdkGLContext.
  8700 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8701 â”‚ â”‚                * It is safe to call this function on a realized #GdkGLContext.
  8702 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the context is realized
  8703 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8704 â”‚ â”‚               realize(): boolean;
  8705 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8706 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets whether the #GdkGLContext should perform extra validations and
  8707 â”‚ â”‚                * run time checking. This is useful during development, but has
  8708 â”‚ â”‚                * additional overhead.
  8709 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8710 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkGLContext must not be realized or made current prior to
  8711 â”‚ â”‚                * calling this function.
  8712 â”‚ â”‚                * @param enabled whether to enable debugging in the context
  8713 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8714 â”‚ â”‚               set_debug_enabled(enabled: boolean): void;
  8715 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8716 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets whether the #GdkGLContext should be forward compatible.
  8717 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8718 â”‚ â”‚                * Forward compatibile contexts must not support OpenGL functionality that
  8719 â”‚ â”‚                * has been marked as deprecated in the requested version; non-forward
  8720 â”‚ â”‚                * compatible contexts, on the other hand, must support both deprecated and
  8721 â”‚ â”‚                * non deprecated functionality.
  8722 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8723 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkGLContext must not be realized or made current prior to calling
  8724 â”‚ â”‚                * this function.
  8725 â”‚ â”‚                * @param compatible whether the context should be forward compatible
  8726 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8727 â”‚ â”‚               set_forward_compatible(compatible: boolean): void;
  8728 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8729 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets the major and minor version of OpenGL to request.
  8730 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8731 â”‚ â”‚                * Setting `major` and `minor` to zero will use the default values.
  8732 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8733 â”‚ â”‚                * The #GdkGLContext must not be realized or made current prior to calling
  8734 â”‚ â”‚                * this function.
  8735 â”‚ â”‚                * @param major the major version to request
  8736 â”‚ â”‚                * @param minor the minor version to request
  8737 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8738 â”‚ â”‚               set_required_version(major: number, minor: number): void;
  8739 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8740 â”‚ â”‚                * Requests that GDK create a OpenGL ES context instead of an OpenGL one,
  8741 â”‚ â”‚                * if the platform and windowing system allows it.
  8742 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8743 â”‚ â”‚                * The `context` must not have been realized.
  8744 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8745 â”‚ â”‚                * By default, GDK will attempt to automatically detect whether the
  8746 â”‚ â”‚                * underlying GL implementation is OpenGL or OpenGL ES once the `context`
  8747 â”‚ â”‚                * is realized.
  8748 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8749 â”‚ â”‚                * You should check the return value of gdk_gl_context_get_use_es() after
  8750 â”‚ â”‚                * calling gdk_gl_context_realize() to decide whether to use the OpenGL or
  8751 â”‚ â”‚                * OpenGL ES API, extensions, or shaders.
  8752 â”‚ â”‚                * @param use_es whether the context should use OpenGL ES instead of OpenGL,   or -1 to allow auto-detection
  8753 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8754 â”‚ â”‚               set_use_es(use_es: number): void;
  8755 â”‚ â”‚           }
  8756 â”‚ â”‚   
  8757 â”‚ â”‚           namespace Keymap {
  8758 â”‚ â”‚               // Signal signatures

  8760 â”‚ â”‚                   'direction-changed': () => void;

  8769 â”‚ â”‚   
  8770 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  8771 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkKeymap defines the translation from keyboard state
  8772 â”‚ â”‚            * (including a hardware key, a modifier mask, and active keyboard group)
  8773 â”‚ â”‚            * to a keyval. This translation has two phases. The first phase is
  8774 â”‚ â”‚            * to determine the effective keyboard group and level for the keyboard
  8775 â”‚ â”‚            * state; the second phase is to look up the keycode/group/level triplet
  8776 â”‚ â”‚            * in the keymap and see what keyval it corresponds to.
  8777 â”‚ â”‚            */
  8778 â”‚ â”‚           class Keymap extends GObject.Object {
  8779 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<Keymap>;
  8780 â”‚ â”‚   
  8781 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8782 â”‚ â”‚                * Compile-time signal type information.
  8783 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8784 â”‚ â”‚                * This instance property is generated only for TypeScript type checking.
  8785 â”‚ â”‚                * It is not defined at runtime and should not be accessed in JS code.
  8786 â”‚ â”‚                * @internal
  8787 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8788 â”‚ â”‚               $signals: Keymap.SignalSignatures;
  8789 â”‚ â”‚   
  8790 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructors
  8791 â”‚ â”‚

  8793 â”‚ â”‚

  8795 â”‚ â”‚   
  8796 â”‚ â”‚               // Signals
  8797 â”‚ â”‚

  8801 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  8802 â”‚ â”‚               connect(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;

  8804 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,

  8808 â”‚ â”‚               emit<K extends keyof Keymap.SignalSignatures>(

  8811 â”‚ â”‚               ): void;

  8816 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  8818 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8819 â”‚ â”‚               static get_default(): Keymap;
  8820 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8821 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the #GdkKeymap attached to `display`.
  8822 â”‚ â”‚                * @param display the #GdkDisplay.
  8823 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8824 â”‚ â”‚               static get_for_display(display: Display): Keymap;
  8825 â”‚ â”‚   
  8826 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
  8827 â”‚ â”‚   
  8828 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8829 â”‚ â”‚                * Maps the non-virtual modifiers (i.e Mod2, Mod3, ...) which are set
  8830 â”‚ â”‚                * in `state` to the virtual modifiers (i.e. Super, Hyper and Meta) and
  8831 â”‚ â”‚                * set the corresponding bits in `state`.
  8832 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8833 â”‚ â”‚                * GDK already does this before delivering key events, but for
  8834 â”‚ â”‚                * compatibility reasons, it only sets the first virtual modifier
  8835 â”‚ â”‚                * it finds, whereas this function sets all matching virtual modifiers.
  8836 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8837 â”‚ â”‚                * This function is useful when matching key events against
  8838 â”‚ â”‚                * accelerators.
  8839 â”‚ â”‚                * @param state pointer to the modifier mask to change
  8840 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8841 â”‚ â”‚               add_virtual_modifiers(state: ModifierType | null): ModifierType;
  8842 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8843 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns whether the Caps Lock modifer is locked.
  8844 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if Caps Lock is on
  8845 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8846 â”‚ â”‚               get_caps_lock_state(): boolean;
  8847 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8848 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the direction of effective layout of the keymap.
  8849 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %PANGO_DIRECTION_LTR or %PANGO_DIRECTION_RTL   if it can determine the direction. %PANGO_DIRECTION_NEUTRAL   otherwise.
  8850 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8851 â”‚ â”‚               get_direction(): Pango.Direction;
  8852 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8853 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the keyvals bound to `hardware_keycode`.
  8854 â”‚ â”‚                * The Nth #GdkKeymapKey in `keys` is bound to the Nth
  8855 â”‚ â”‚                * keyval in `keyvals`. Free the returned arrays with g_free().
  8856 â”‚ â”‚                * When a keycode is pressed by the user, the keyval from
  8857 â”‚ â”‚                * this list of entries is selected by considering the effective
  8858 â”‚ â”‚                * keyboard group and level. See gdk_keymap_translate_keyboard_state().
  8859 â”‚ â”‚                * @param hardware_keycode a keycode
  8860 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if there were any entries
  8861 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8862 â”‚ â”‚               get_entries_for_keycode(hardware_keycode: number): [boolean, KeymapKey[] | null, number[] | null];
  8863 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8864 â”‚ â”‚                * Obtains a list of keycode/group/level combinations that will
  8865 â”‚ â”‚                * generate `keyval`. Groups and levels are two kinds of keyboard mode;
  8866 â”‚ â”‚                * in general, the level determines whether the top or bottom symbol
  8867 â”‚ â”‚                * on a key is used, and the group determines whether the left or
  8868 â”‚ â”‚                * right symbol is used. On US keyboards, the shift key changes the
  8869 â”‚ â”‚                * keyboard level, and there are no groups. A group switch key might
  8870 â”‚ â”‚                * convert a keyboard between Hebrew to English modes, for example.
  8871 â”‚ â”‚                * #GdkEventKey contains a %group field that indicates the active
  8872 â”‚ â”‚                * keyboard group. The level is computed from the modifier mask.
  8873 â”‚ â”‚                * The returned array should be freed
  8874 â”‚ â”‚                * with g_free().
  8875 â”‚ â”‚                * @param keyval a keyval, such as %GDK_KEY_a, %GDK_KEY_Up, %GDK_KEY_Return, etc.
  8876 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if keys were found and returned
  8877 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8878 â”‚ â”‚               get_entries_for_keyval(keyval: number): [boolean, KeymapKey[]];
  8879 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8880 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the modifier mask the `keymapâ€™`s windowing system backend
  8881 â”‚ â”‚                * uses for a particular purpose.
  8882 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8883 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that this function always returns real hardware modifiers, not
  8884 â”‚ â”‚                * virtual ones (e.g. it will return #GDK_MOD1_MASK rather than
  8885 â”‚ â”‚                * #GDK_META_MASK if the backend maps MOD1 to META), so there are use
  8886 â”‚ â”‚                * cases where the return value of this function has to be transformed
  8887 â”‚ â”‚                * by gdk_keymap_add_virtual_modifiers() in order to contain the
  8888 â”‚ â”‚                * expected result.
  8889 â”‚ â”‚                * @param intent the use case for the modifier mask
  8890 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the modifier mask used for @intent.
  8891 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8892 â”‚ â”‚               get_modifier_mask(intent: ModifierIntent | null): ModifierType;
  8893 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8894 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the current modifier state.
  8895 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the current modifier state.
  8896 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8897 â”‚ â”‚               get_modifier_state(): number;
  8898 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8899 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns whether the Num Lock modifer is locked.
  8900 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if Num Lock is on
  8901 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8902 â”‚ â”‚               get_num_lock_state(): boolean;
  8903 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8904 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns whether the Scroll Lock modifer is locked.
  8905 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if Scroll Lock is on
  8906 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8907 â”‚ â”‚               get_scroll_lock_state(): boolean;
  8908 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8909 â”‚ â”‚                * Determines if keyboard layouts for both right-to-left and left-to-right
  8910 â”‚ â”‚                * languages are in use.
  8911 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if there are layouts in both directions, %FALSE otherwise
  8912 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8913 â”‚ â”‚               have_bidi_layouts(): boolean;
  8914 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8915 â”‚ â”‚                * Looks up the keyval mapped to a keycode/group/level triplet.
  8916 â”‚ â”‚                * If no keyval is bound to `key,` returns 0. For normal user input,
  8917 â”‚ â”‚                * you want to use gdk_keymap_translate_keyboard_state() instead of
  8918 â”‚ â”‚                * this function, since the effective group/level may not be
  8919 â”‚ â”‚                * the same as the current keyboard state.
  8920 â”‚ â”‚                * @param key a #GdkKeymapKey with keycode, group, and level initialized
  8921 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a keyval, or 0 if none was mapped to the given @key
  8922 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8923 â”‚ â”‚               lookup_key(key: KeymapKey): number;
  8924 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8925 â”‚ â”‚                * Maps the virtual modifiers (i.e. Super, Hyper and Meta) which
  8926 â”‚ â”‚                * are set in `state` to their non-virtual counterparts (i.e. Mod2,
  8927 â”‚ â”‚                * Mod3,...) and set the corresponding bits in `state`.
  8928 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8929 â”‚ â”‚                * This function is useful when matching key events against
  8930 â”‚ â”‚                * accelerators.
  8931 â”‚ â”‚                * @param state pointer to the modifier state to map
  8932 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %FALSE if two virtual modifiers were mapped to the     same non-virtual modifier. Note that %FALSE is also returned     if a virtual modifier is mapped to a non-virtual modifier that     was already set in @state.
  8933 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8934 â”‚ â”‚               map_virtual_modifiers(state: ModifierType | null): [boolean, ModifierType];
  8935 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  8936 â”‚ â”‚                * Translates the contents of a #GdkEventKey into a keyval, effective
  8937 â”‚ â”‚                * group, and level. Modifiers that affected the translation and
  8938 â”‚ â”‚                * are thus unavailable for application use are returned in
  8939 â”‚ â”‚                * `consumed_modifiers`.
  8940 â”‚ â”‚                * See [Groups][key-group-explanation] for an explanation of
  8941 â”‚ â”‚                * groups and levels. The `effective_group` is the group that was
  8942 â”‚ â”‚                * actually used for the translation; some keys such as Enter are not
  8943 â”‚ â”‚                * affected by the active keyboard group. The `level` is derived from
  8944 â”‚ â”‚                * `state`. For convenience, #GdkEventKey already contains the translated
  8945 â”‚ â”‚                * keyval, so this function isnâ€™t as useful as you might think.
  8946 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8947 â”‚ â”‚                * `consumed_modifiers` gives modifiers that should be masked outfrom `state`
  8948 â”‚ â”‚                * when comparing this key press to a hot key. For instance, on a US keyboard,
  8949 â”‚ â”‚                * the `plus` symbol is shifted, so when comparing a key press to a
  8950 â”‚ â”‚                * `<Control>plus` accelerator `<Shift>` should be masked out.
  8951 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8952 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8953 â”‚ â”‚                * ```c
  8954 â”‚ â”‚                * // We want to ignore irrelevant modifiers like ScrollLock
  8955 â”‚ â”‚                * #define ALL_ACCELS_MASK (GDK_CONTROL_MASK | GDK_SHIFT_MASK | GDK_MOD1_MASK)
  8956 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_keymap_translate_keyboard_state (keymap, event->hardware_keycode,
  8957 â”‚ â”‚                *                                      event->state, event->group,
  8958 â”‚ â”‚                *                                      &keyval, NULL, NULL, &consumed);
  8959 â”‚ â”‚                * if (keyval == GDK_PLUS &&
  8960 â”‚ â”‚                *     (event->state & ~consumed & ALL_ACCELS_MASK) == GDK_CONTROL_MASK)
  8961 â”‚ â”‚                *   // Control was pressed
  8962 â”‚ â”‚                * ```
  8963 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8964 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8965 â”‚ â”‚                * An older interpretation `consumed_modifiers` was that it contained
  8966 â”‚ â”‚                * all modifiers that might affect the translation of the key;
  8967 â”‚ â”‚                * this allowed accelerators to be stored with irrelevant consumed
  8968 â”‚ â”‚                * modifiers, by doing:
  8969 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8970 â”‚ â”‚                * ```c
  8971 â”‚ â”‚                * // XXX Donâ€™t do this XXX
  8972 â”‚ â”‚                * if (keyval == accel_keyval &&
  8973 â”‚ â”‚                *     (event->state & ~consumed & ALL_ACCELS_MASK) == (accel_mods & ~consumed))
  8974 â”‚ â”‚                *   // Accelerator was pressed
  8975 â”‚ â”‚                * ```
  8976 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8977 â”‚ â”‚                *
  8978 â”‚ â”‚                * However, this did not work if multi-modifier combinations were
  8979 â”‚ â”‚                * used in the keymap, since, for instance, `<Control>` would be
  8980 â”‚ â”‚                * masked out even if only `<Control><Alt>` was used in the keymap.
  8981 â”‚ â”‚                * To support this usage as well as well as possible, all single
  8982 â”‚ â”‚                * modifier combinations that could affect the key for any combination
  8983 â”‚ â”‚                * of modifiers will be returned in `consumed_modifiers;` multi-modifier
  8984 â”‚ â”‚                * combinations are returned only when actually found in `state`. When
  8985 â”‚ â”‚                * you store accelerators, you should always store them with consumed
  8986 â”‚ â”‚                * modifiers removed. Store `<Control>plus`, not `<Control><Shift>plus`,
  8987 â”‚ â”‚                * @param hardware_keycode a keycode
  8988 â”‚ â”‚                * @param state a modifier state
  8989 â”‚ â”‚                * @param group active keyboard group
  8990 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if there was a keyval bound to the keycode/state/group
  8991 â”‚ â”‚                */
  8992 â”‚ â”‚               translate_keyboard_state(
  8993 â”‚ â”‚                   hardware_keycode: number,
  8994 â”‚ â”‚                   state: ModifierType | null,
  8995 â”‚ â”‚                   group: number,
  8996 â”‚ â”‚               ): [boolean, number, number, number, ModifierType | null];
  8997 â”‚ â”‚           }
  8998 â”‚ â”‚

  9036 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  9037 â”‚ â”‚            * GdkMonitor objects represent the individual outputs that are
  9038 â”‚ â”‚            * associated with a #GdkDisplay. GdkDisplay has APIs to enumerate
  9039 â”‚ â”‚            * monitors with gdk_display_get_n_monitors() and gdk_display_get_monitor(), and

  9041 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_display_get_monitor_at_window().

  9044 â”‚ â”‚            * APIs in GdkScreen to obtain monitor-related information.
  9045 â”‚ â”‚            */

  9086 â”‚ â”‚                   callback: GObject.SignalCallback<this, Monitor.SignalSignatures[K]>,
  9087 â”‚ â”‚               ): number;
  9088 â”‚ â”‚               connect(signal: string, callback: (...args: any[]) => any): number;
  9089 â”‚ â”‚               connect_after<K extends keyof Monitor.SignalSignatures>(
  9090 â”‚ â”‚                   signal: K,

  9107 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  9137 â”‚ â”‚                * is returned as 60000.

  9141 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  9145 â”‚ â”‚                *

  9147 â”‚ â”‚                * particular monitor, but most of the time youâ€™re drawing to a window

  9150 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9155 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the subpixel layout
  9156 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9161 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9163 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9164 â”‚ â”‚                * Retrieves the size and position of the â€œwork areaâ€ on a monitor

  9166 â”‚ â”‚                * â€application pixelsâ€, not in â€device pixelsâ€ (see

  9176 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9182 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9205 â”‚ â”‚           /**
  9206 â”‚ â”‚            * #GdkScreen objects are the GDK representation of the screen on
  9207 â”‚ â”‚            * which windows can be displayed and on which the pointer moves.
  9208 â”‚ â”‚            * X originally identified screens with physical screens, but
  9209 â”‚ â”‚            * nowadays it is more common to have a single #GdkScreen which
  9210 â”‚ â”‚            * combines several physical monitors (see gdk_screen_get_n_monitors()).
  9211 â”‚ â”‚            *
  9212 â”‚ â”‚            * GdkScreen is used throughout GDK and GTK+ to specify which screen
  9213 â”‚ â”‚            * the top level windows are to be displayed on. it is also used to
  9214 â”‚ â”‚            * query the screen specification and default settings such as
  9215 â”‚ â”‚            * the default visual (gdk_screen_get_system_visual()), the dimensions
  9216 â”‚ â”‚            * of the physical monitors (gdk_screen_get_monitor_geometry()), etc.
  9217 â”‚ â”‚            */

  9445 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9447 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9448 â”‚ â”‚                * Gets a visual to use for creating windows with an alpha channel.
  9449 â”‚ â”‚                * The windowing system on which GTK+ is running
  9450 â”‚ â”‚                * may not support this capability, in which case %NULL will
  9451 â”‚ â”‚                * be returned. Even if a non-%NULL value is returned, its
  9452 â”‚ â”‚                * possible that the windowâ€™s alpha channel wonâ€™t be honored

  9513 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9514 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns a #GList of #GdkWindows representing the current
  9515 â”‚ â”‚                * window stack.
  9516 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9517 â”‚ â”‚                * On X11, this is done by inspecting the _NET_CLIENT_LIST_STACKING
  9518 â”‚ â”‚                * property on the root window, as described in the
  9519 â”‚ â”‚                * [Extended Window Manager Hints](http://www.freedesktop.org/Standards/wm-spec).
  9520 â”‚ â”‚                * If the window manager does not support the
  9521 â”‚ â”‚                * _NET_CLIENT_LIST_STACKING hint, this function returns %NULL.
  9522 â”‚ â”‚                *

  9641 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
  9642 â”‚ â”‚   
  9643 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9644 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the capabilities this #GdkSeat currently has.
  9645 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the seat capabilities
  9646 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9651 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9656 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9658 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9659 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the master device that routes pointer events.
  9660 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a master #GdkDevice with pointer          capabilities. This object is owned by GTK+ and must not be freed.
  9661 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9662 â”‚ â”‚               get_pointer(): Device | null;
  9663 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9664 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the slave devices that match the given capabilities.
  9665 â”‚ â”‚                * @param capabilities capabilities to get devices for
  9666 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns A list of #GdkDevices.          The list must be freed with g_list_free(), the elements are owned          by GDK and must not be freed.
  9667 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9668 â”‚ â”‚               get_slaves(capabilities: SeatCapabilities | null): Device[];
  9669 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9670 â”‚ â”‚                * Grabs the seat so that all events corresponding to the given `capabilities`
  9671 â”‚ â”‚                * are passed to this application until the seat is ungrabbed with gdk_seat_ungrab(),
  9672 â”‚ â”‚                * or the window becomes hidden. This overrides any previous grab on the
  9673 â”‚ â”‚                * seat by this client.
  9674 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9675 â”‚ â”‚                * As a rule of thumb, if a grab is desired over %GDK_SEAT_CAPABILITY_POINTER,
  9676 â”‚ â”‚                * all other "pointing" capabilities (eg. %GDK_SEAT_CAPABILITY_TOUCH) should
  9677 â”‚ â”‚                * be grabbed too, so the user is able to interact with all of those while
  9678 â”‚ â”‚                * the grab holds, you should thus use %GDK_SEAT_CAPABILITY_ALL_POINTING most
  9679 â”‚ â”‚                * commonly.
  9680 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9681 â”‚ â”‚                * Grabs are used for operations which need complete control over the
  9682 â”‚ â”‚                * events corresponding to the given capabilities. For example in GTK+ this
  9683 â”‚ â”‚                * is used for Drag and Drop operations, popup menus and such.
  9684 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9685 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that if the event mask of a #GdkWindow has selected both button press
  9686 â”‚ â”‚                * and button release events, or touch begin and touch end, then a press event
  9687 â”‚ â”‚                * will cause an automatic grab until the button is released, equivalent to a
  9688 â”‚ â”‚                * grab on the window with `owner_events` set to %TRUE. This is done because most
  9689 â”‚ â”‚                * applications expect to receive paired press and release events.
  9690 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9691 â”‚ â”‚                * If you set up anything at the time you take the grab that needs to be
  9692 â”‚ â”‚                * cleaned up when the grab ends, you should handle the #GdkEventGrabBroken
  9693 â”‚ â”‚                * events that are emitted when the grab ends unvoluntarily.
  9694 â”‚ â”‚                * @param window the #GdkWindow which will own the grab
  9695 â”‚ â”‚                * @param capabilities capabilities that will be grabbed
  9696 â”‚ â”‚                * @param owner_events if %FALSE then all device events are reported with respect to                @window and are only reported if selected by @event_mask. If                %TRUE then pointer events for this application are reported                as normal, but pointer events outside this application are                reported with respect to @window and only if selected by                @event_mask. In either mode, unreported events are discarded.
  9697 â”‚ â”‚                * @param cursor the cursor to display while the grab is active. If          this is %NULL then the normal cursors are used for          @window and its descendants, and the cursor for @window is used          elsewhere.
  9698 â”‚ â”‚                * @param event the event that is triggering the grab, or %NULL if none         is available.
  9699 â”‚ â”‚                * @param prepare_func function to                prepare the window to be grabbed, it can be %NULL if @window is                visible before this call.
  9700 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %GDK_GRAB_SUCCESS if the grab was successful.
  9701 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9702 â”‚ â”‚               grab(
  9703 â”‚ â”‚                   window: Window,
  9704 â”‚ â”‚                   capabilities: SeatCapabilities | null,
  9705 â”‚ â”‚                   owner_events: boolean,
  9706 â”‚ â”‚                   cursor?: Cursor | null,
  9707 â”‚ â”‚                   event?: Event | null,
  9708 â”‚ â”‚                   prepare_func?: SeatGrabPrepareFunc | null,
  9709 â”‚ â”‚               ): GrabStatus;
  9710 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9711 â”‚ â”‚                * Releases a grab added through gdk_seat_grab().
  9712 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9713 â”‚ â”‚               ungrab(): void;
  9714 â”‚ â”‚           }

  9767 â”‚ â”‚               /**

  9780 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9782 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9783 â”‚ â”‚                * Combines gdk_visual_get_best_with_depth() and
  9784 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_visual_get_best_with_type().

  9787 â”‚ â”‚                */

  9789 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9790 â”‚ â”‚                * Get the best visual with depth `depth` for the default GDK screen.
  9791 â”‚ â”‚                * Color visuals and visuals with mutable colormaps are preferred
  9792 â”‚ â”‚                * over grayscale or fixed-colormap visuals. The return value should
  9793 â”‚ â”‚                * not be freed. %NULL may be returned if no visual supports `depth`.
  9794 â”‚ â”‚                * @param depth a bit depth
  9795 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9796 â”‚ â”‚               static get_best_with_depth(depth: number): Visual;
