  9973 â”‚ â”‚               ): [number, number];
  9974 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9975 â”‚ â”‚                * Calls gdk_window_process_updates() for all windows (see #GdkWindow)
  9976 â”‚ â”‚                * in the application.
  9977 â”‚ â”‚                */
  9978 â”‚ â”‚               static process_all_updates(): void;
  9979 â”‚ â”‚               /**
  9980 â”‚ â”‚                * With update debugging enabled, calls to
  9981 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_invalidate_region() clear the invalidated region of the
  9982 â”‚ â”‚                * screen to a noticeable color, and GDK pauses for a short time
  9983 â”‚ â”‚                * before sending exposes to windows during
  9984 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_process_updates().  The net effect is that you can see
  9985 â”‚ â”‚                * the invalid region for each window and watch redraws as they
  9986 â”‚ â”‚                * occur. This allows you to diagnose inefficiencies in your application.
  9987 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9988 â”‚ â”‚                * In essence, because the GDK rendering model prevents all flicker,
  9989 â”‚ â”‚                * if you are redrawing the same region 400 times you may never
  9990 â”‚ â”‚                * notice, aside from noticing a speed problem. Enabling update
  9991 â”‚ â”‚                * debugging causes GTK to flicker slowly and noticeably, so you can
  9992 â”‚ â”‚                * see exactly whatâ€™s being redrawn when, in what order.
  9993 â”‚ â”‚                *
  9994 â”‚ â”‚                * The --gtk-debug=updates command line option passed to GTK+ programs
  9995 â”‚ â”‚                * enables this debug option at application startup time. That's
  9996 â”‚ â”‚                * usually more useful than calling gdk_window_set_debug_updates()
  9997 â”‚ â”‚                * yourself, though you might want to use this function to enable
  9998 â”‚ â”‚                * updates sometime after application startup time.
  9999 â”‚ â”‚                * @param setting %TRUE to turn on update debugging
 10000 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10001 â”‚ â”‚               static set_debug_updates(setting: boolean): void;
 10002 â”‚ â”‚   
 10003 â”‚ â”‚               // Virtual methods
 10004 â”‚ â”‚   
 10005 â”‚ â”‚               vfunc_create_surface(width: number, height: number): cairo.Surface;
 10006 â”‚ â”‚               vfunc_from_embedder(embedder_x: number, embedder_y: number, offscreen_x: number, offscreen_y: number): void;
 10007 â”‚ â”‚               vfunc_to_embedder(offscreen_x: number, offscreen_y: number, embedder_x: number, embedder_y: number): void;
 10008 â”‚ â”‚   
 10009 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
 10010 â”‚ â”‚   
 10011 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10012 â”‚ â”‚                * Emits a short beep associated to `window` in the appropriate
 10013 â”‚ â”‚                * display, if supported. Otherwise, emits a short beep on
 10014 â”‚ â”‚                * the display just as gdk_display_beep().
 10015 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10016 â”‚ â”‚               beep(): void;
 10017 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10018 â”‚ â”‚                * Indicates that you are beginning the process of redrawing `region`
 10019 â”‚ â”‚                * on `window,` and provides you with a #GdkDrawingContext.
 10020 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10021 â”‚ â”‚                * If `window` is a top level #GdkWindow, backed by a native window
 10022 â”‚ â”‚                * implementation, a backing store (offscreen buffer) large enough to
 10023 â”‚ â”‚                * contain `region` will be created. The backing store will be initialized
 10024 â”‚ â”‚                * with the background color or background surface for `window`. Then, all
 10025 â”‚ â”‚                * drawing operations performed on `window` will be diverted to the
 10026 â”‚ â”‚                * backing store. When you call gdk_window_end_frame(), the contents of
 10027 â”‚ â”‚                * the backing store will be copied to `window,` making it visible
 10028 â”‚ â”‚                * on screen. Only the part of `window` contained in `region` will be
 10029 â”‚ â”‚                * modified; that is, drawing operations are clipped to `region`.
 10030 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10031 â”‚ â”‚                * The net result of all this is to remove flicker, because the user
 10032 â”‚ â”‚                * sees the finished product appear all at once when you call
 10033 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_end_draw_frame(). If you draw to `window` directly without
 10034 â”‚ â”‚                * calling gdk_window_begin_draw_frame(), the user may see flicker
 10035 â”‚ â”‚                * as individual drawing operations are performed in sequence.
 10036 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10037 â”‚ â”‚                * When using GTK+, the widget system automatically places calls to
 10038 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_draw_frame() and gdk_window_end_draw_frame() around
 10039 â”‚ â”‚                * emissions of the `GtkWidget::draw` signal. That is, if youâ€™re
 10040 â”‚ â”‚                * drawing the contents of the widget yourself, you can assume that the
 10041 â”‚ â”‚                * widget has a cleared background, is already set as the clip region,
 10042 â”‚ â”‚                * and already has a backing store. Therefore in most cases, application
 10043 â”‚ â”‚                * code in GTK does not need to call gdk_window_begin_draw_frame()
 10044 â”‚ â”‚                * explicitly.
 10045 â”‚ â”‚                * @param region a Cairo region
 10046 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a #GdkDrawingContext context that should be   used to draw the contents of the window; the returned context is owned   by GDK.
 10047 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10048 â”‚ â”‚               begin_draw_frame(region: cairo.Region): DrawingContext;
 10049 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10050 â”‚ â”‚                * Begins a window move operation (for a toplevel window).
 10051 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10052 â”‚ â”‚                * This function assumes that the drag is controlled by the
 10053 â”‚ â”‚                * client pointer device, use gdk_window_begin_move_drag_for_device()
 10054 â”‚ â”‚                * to begin a drag with a different device.
 10055 â”‚ â”‚                * @param button the button being used to drag, or 0 for a keyboard-initiated drag
 10056 â”‚ â”‚                * @param root_x root window X coordinate of mouse click that began the drag
 10057 â”‚ â”‚                * @param root_y root window Y coordinate of mouse click that began the drag
 10058 â”‚ â”‚                * @param timestamp timestamp of mouse click that began the drag
 10059 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10060 â”‚ â”‚               begin_move_drag(button: number, root_x: number, root_y: number, timestamp: number): void;
 10061 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10062 â”‚ â”‚                * Begins a window move operation (for a toplevel window).
 10063 â”‚ â”‚                * You might use this function to implement a â€œwindow move grip,â€ for
 10064 â”‚ â”‚                * example. The function works best with window managers that support the
 10065 â”‚ â”‚                * [Extended Window Manager Hints](http://www.freedesktop.org/Standards/wm-spec)
 10066 â”‚ â”‚                * but has a fallback implementation for other window managers.
 10067 â”‚ â”‚                * @param device the device used for the operation
 10068 â”‚ â”‚                * @param button the button being used to drag, or 0 for a keyboard-initiated drag
 10069 â”‚ â”‚                * @param root_x root window X coordinate of mouse click that began the drag
 10070 â”‚ â”‚                * @param root_y root window Y coordinate of mouse click that began the drag
 10071 â”‚ â”‚                * @param timestamp timestamp of mouse click that began the drag
 10072 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10073 â”‚ â”‚               begin_move_drag_for_device(
 10074 â”‚ â”‚                   device: Device,
 10075 â”‚ â”‚                   button: number,
 10076 â”‚ â”‚                   root_x: number,
 10077 â”‚ â”‚                   root_y: number,
 10078 â”‚ â”‚                   timestamp: number,
 10079 â”‚ â”‚               ): void;
 10080 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10081 â”‚ â”‚                * A convenience wrapper around gdk_window_begin_paint_region() which
 10082 â”‚ â”‚                * creates a rectangular region for you. See
 10083 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_paint_region() for details.
 10084 â”‚ â”‚                * @param rectangle rectangle you intend to draw to
 10085 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10086 â”‚ â”‚               begin_paint_rect(rectangle: Rectangle): void;
 10087 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10088 â”‚ â”‚                * Indicates that you are beginning the process of redrawing `region`.
 10089 â”‚ â”‚                * A backing store (offscreen buffer) large enough to contain `region`
 10090 â”‚ â”‚                * will be created. The backing store will be initialized with the
 10091 â”‚ â”‚                * background color or background surface for `window`. Then, all
 10092 â”‚ â”‚                * drawing operations performed on `window` will be diverted to the
 10093 â”‚ â”‚                * backing store.  When you call gdk_window_end_paint(), the backing
 10094 â”‚ â”‚                * store will be copied to `window,` making it visible onscreen. Only
 10095 â”‚ â”‚                * the part of `window` contained in `region` will be modified; that is,
 10096 â”‚ â”‚                * drawing operations are clipped to `region`.
 10097 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10098 â”‚ â”‚                * The net result of all this is to remove flicker, because the user
 10099 â”‚ â”‚                * sees the finished product appear all at once when you call
 10100 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_end_paint(). If you draw to `window` directly without
 10101 â”‚ â”‚                * calling gdk_window_begin_paint_region(), the user may see flicker
 10102 â”‚ â”‚                * as individual drawing operations are performed in sequence.  The
 10103 â”‚ â”‚                * clipping and background-initializing features of
 10104 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_paint_region() are conveniences for the
 10105 â”‚ â”‚                * programmer, so you can avoid doing that work yourself.
 10106 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10107 â”‚ â”‚                * When using GTK+, the widget system automatically places calls to
 10108 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_paint_region() and gdk_window_end_paint() around
 10109 â”‚ â”‚                * emissions of the expose_event signal. That is, if youâ€™re writing an
 10110 â”‚ â”‚                * expose event handler, you can assume that the exposed area in
 10111 â”‚ â”‚                * #GdkEventExpose has already been cleared to the window background,
 10112 â”‚ â”‚                * is already set as the clip region, and already has a backing store.
 10113 â”‚ â”‚                * Therefore in most cases, application code need not call
 10114 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_paint_region(). (You can disable the automatic
 10115 â”‚ â”‚                * calls around expose events on a widget-by-widget basis by calling
 10116 â”‚ â”‚                * gtk_widget_set_double_buffered().)
 10117 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10118 â”‚ â”‚                * If you call this function multiple times before calling the
 10119 â”‚ â”‚                * matching gdk_window_end_paint(), the backing stores are pushed onto
 10120 â”‚ â”‚                * a stack. gdk_window_end_paint() copies the topmost backing store
 10121 â”‚ â”‚                * onscreen, subtracts the topmost region from all other regions in
 10122 â”‚ â”‚                * the stack, and pops the stack. All drawing operations affect only
 10123 â”‚ â”‚                * the topmost backing store in the stack. One matching call to
 10124 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_end_paint() is required for each call to
 10125 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_window_begin_paint_region().
 10126 â”‚ â”‚                * @param region region you intend to draw to
 10127 â”‚ â”‚                */
 10128 â”‚ â”‚               begin_paint_region(region: cairo.Region): void;
 10129 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 10130 â”‚ â”‚                * Begins a window resize operation (for a toplevel window).
 10131 â”‚ â”‚                *
 10132 â”‚ â”‚                * This function assumes that the drag is controlled by the
 10133 â”‚ â”‚                * client pointer device, use gdk_window_begin_resize_drag_for_device()
 10134 â”‚ â”‚                * to begin a drag with a different device.
 10135 â”‚ â”‚                * @param edge the edge or corner from which the drag is started

 11467 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 11469 â”‚ â”‚                * below.
 11470 â”‚ â”‚                *
 11471 â”‚ â”‚                * The default value of this is %FALSE, which means that pointer
 11472 â”‚ â”‚                * events that happen inside the window are send first to the window,
 11473 â”‚ â”‚                * but if the event is not selected by the event mask then the event
 11474 â”‚ â”‚                * is sent to the parent window, and so on up the hierarchy.

 11477 â”‚ â”‚                * window wasn't there at all, and thus will be sent first to any
 11478 â”‚ â”‚                * windows below `window`. This is useful if the window is used in a

 11480 â”‚ â”‚                * "pointer-events: none".

 11484 â”‚ â”‚                * that cases you would get the in-between related events such as the pointer

 11494 â”‚ â”‚                * distinguish it from other kinds of window in the same application.
 11495 â”‚ â”‚                * When an application is restarted after being saved in a previous
 11496 â”‚ â”‚                * session, all windows with the same title and role are treated as
 11497 â”‚ â”‚                * interchangeable.  So if you have two windows with the same title
 11498 â”‚ â”‚                * that should be distinguished for session management purposes, you

 11509 â”‚ â”‚                * to know where the extents of the actual frame lie, so that users

 11882 â”‚ â”‚            * Used for button press and button release events. The
 11883 â”‚ â”‚            * `type` field will be one of %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS,
 11884 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS, %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS or %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE,
 11885 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11886 â”‚ â”‚            * Double and triple-clicks result in a sequence of events being received.
 11887 â”‚ â”‚            * For double-clicks the order of events will be:
 11888 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11889 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 11890 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE
 11891 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 11892 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS
 11893 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE
 11894 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11895 â”‚ â”‚            * Note that the first click is received just like a normal
 11896 â”‚ â”‚            * button press, while the second click results in a %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS
 11897 â”‚ â”‚            * being received just after the %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS.
 11898 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11899 â”‚ â”‚            * Triple-clicks are very similar to double-clicks, except that
 11900 â”‚ â”‚            * %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS is inserted after the third click. The order of the
 11901 â”‚ â”‚            * events is:
 11902 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11903 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 11904 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE
 11905 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 11906 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_2BUTTON_PRESS
 11907 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE
 11908 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 11909 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_3BUTTON_PRESS
 11910 â”‚ â”‚            * - %GDK_BUTTON_RELEASE
 11911 â”‚ â”‚            *
 11912 â”‚ â”‚            * For a double click to occur, the second button press must occur within
 11913 â”‚ â”‚            * 1/4 of a second of the first. For a triple click to occur, the third
 11914 â”‚ â”‚            * button press must also occur within 1/2 second of the first button press.
 11915 â”‚ â”‚            */
 11916 â”‚ â”‚           class EventButton {
 11917 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<EventButton>;
 11918 â”‚ â”‚   
 11919 â”‚ â”‚               // Fields
 11920 â”‚ â”‚   
 11921 â”‚ â”‚               type: EventType;
 11922 â”‚ â”‚               window: Window;
 11923 â”‚ â”‚               send_event: number;

 11925 â”‚ â”‚               x: number;

 12472 â”‚ â”‚           /**

 12476 â”‚ â”‚            * The information in #GdkFrameTimings is useful for precise synchronization
 12477 â”‚ â”‚            * of video with the event or audio streams, and for measuring
 12478 â”‚ â”‚            * quality metrics for the applicationâ€™s display, such as latency and jitter.
 12479 â”‚ â”‚            */
 12480 â”‚ â”‚           abstract class FrameTimings {
 12481 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<FrameTimings>;

 12493 â”‚ â”‚                * accessor functions for #GdkFrameTimings can return 0 to

 12500 â”‚ â”‚                */

 12502 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 12505 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns the frame counter value for this frame
 12506 â”‚ â”‚                */

 12515 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 12517 â”‚ â”‚                * no predicted time may be available, if one is available, it will
 12518 â”‚ â”‚                * be available while the frame is being generated, in contrast to
 12519 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_frame_timings_get_presentation_time(), which is only available

 12521 â”‚ â”‚                * animating, you should use gdk_frame_clock_get_frame_time() rather

 12534 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 12539 â”‚ â”‚                */

 12553 â”‚ â”‚           /**
 12554 â”‚ â”‚            * The #GdkGeometry struct gives the window manager information about
 12555 â”‚ â”‚            * a windowâ€™s geometry constraints. Normally you would set these on
 12556 â”‚ â”‚            * the GTK+ level using gtk_window_set_geometry_hints(). #GtkWindow
 12557 â”‚ â”‚            * then sets the hints on the #GdkWindow it creates.
 12558 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12559 â”‚ â”‚            * gdk_window_set_geometry_hints() expects the hints to be fully valid already
 12560 â”‚ â”‚            * and simply passes them to the window manager; in contrast,
 12561 â”‚ â”‚            * gtk_window_set_geometry_hints() performs some interpretation. For example,
 12562 â”‚ â”‚            * #GtkWindow will apply the hints to the geometry widget instead of the
 12563 â”‚ â”‚            * toplevel window, if you set a geometry widget. Also, the
 12564 â”‚ â”‚            * `min_width/``min_height/``max_width/``max_height` fields may be set to -1, and
 12565 â”‚ â”‚            * #GtkWindow will substitute the size request of the window or geometry widget.
 12566 â”‚ â”‚            * If the minimum size hint is not provided, #GtkWindow will use its requisition
 12567 â”‚ â”‚            * as the minimum size. If the minimum size is provided and a geometry widget is
 12568 â”‚ â”‚            * set, #GtkWindow will take the minimum size as the minimum size of the
 12569 â”‚ â”‚            * geometry widget rather than the entire window. The base size is treated
 12570 â”‚ â”‚            * similarly.
 12571 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12572 â”‚ â”‚            * The canonical use-case for gtk_window_set_geometry_hints() is to get a
 12573 â”‚ â”‚            * terminal widget to resize properly. Here, the terminal text area should be
 12574 â”‚ â”‚            * the geometry widget; #GtkWindow will then automatically set the base size to
 12575 â”‚ â”‚            * the size of other widgets in the terminal window, such as the menubar and
 12576 â”‚ â”‚            * scrollbar. Then, the `width_inc` and `height_inc` fields should be set to the
 12577 â”‚ â”‚            * size of one character in the terminal. Finally, the base size should be set
 12578 â”‚ â”‚            * to the size of one character. The net effect is that the minimum size of the
 12579 â”‚ â”‚            * terminal will have a 1x1 character terminal area, and only terminal sizes on
 12580 â”‚ â”‚            * the â€œcharacter gridâ€ will be allowed.
 12581 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12582 â”‚ â”‚            * Hereâ€™s an example of how the terminal example would be implemented, assuming
 12583 â”‚ â”‚            * a terminal area widget called â€œterminalâ€ and a toplevel window â€œtoplevelâ€:
 12584 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12585 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12586 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
 12587 â”‚ â”‚            *  GdkGeometry hints;
 12588 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12589 â”‚ â”‚            *  hints.base_width = terminal->char_width;
 12590 â”‚ â”‚            *         hints.base_height = terminal->char_height;
 12591 â”‚ â”‚            *         hints.min_width = terminal->char_width;
 12592 â”‚ â”‚            *         hints.min_height = terminal->char_height;
 12593 â”‚ â”‚            *         hints.width_inc = terminal->char_width;
 12594 â”‚ â”‚            *         hints.height_inc = terminal->char_height;
 12595 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12596 â”‚ â”‚            *  gtk_window_set_geometry_hints (GTK_WINDOW (toplevel),
 12597 â”‚ â”‚            *                                 GTK_WIDGET (terminal),
 12598 â”‚ â”‚            *                                 &hints,
 12599 â”‚ â”‚            *                                 GDK_HINT_RESIZE_INC |
 12600 â”‚ â”‚            *                                 GDK_HINT_MIN_SIZE |
 12601 â”‚ â”‚            *                                 GDK_HINT_BASE_SIZE);
 12602 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
 12603 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12604 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12605 â”‚ â”‚            * The other useful fields are the `min_aspect` and `max_aspect` fields; these
 12606 â”‚ â”‚            * contain a width/height ratio as a floating point number. If a geometry widget
 12607 â”‚ â”‚            * is set, the aspect applies to the geometry widget rather than the entire
 12608 â”‚ â”‚            * window. The most common use of these hints is probably to set `min_aspect` and
 12609 â”‚ â”‚            * `max_aspect` to the same value, thus forcing the window to keep a constant
 12610 â”‚ â”‚            * aspect ratio.
 12611 â”‚ â”‚            */
 12612 â”‚ â”‚           class Geometry {
 12613 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<Geometry>;
 12614 â”‚ â”‚   
 12615 â”‚ â”‚               // Fields
 12616 â”‚ â”‚   
 12617 â”‚ â”‚               min_width: number;
 12618 â”‚ â”‚               min_height: number;

 12735 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12736 â”‚ â”‚                * The string can be either one of:
 12737 â”‚ â”‚                * - A standard name (Taken from the X11 rgb.txt file).
 12738 â”‚ â”‚                * - A hexadecimal value in the form â€œ\#rgbâ€, â€œ\#rrggbbâ€,
 12739 â”‚ â”‚                *   â€œ\#rrrgggbbbâ€ or â€\#rrrrggggbbbbâ€
 12740 â”‚ â”‚                * - A RGB color in the form â€œrgb(r,g,b)â€ (In this case the color will
 12741 â”‚ â”‚                *   have full opacity)
 12742 â”‚ â”‚                * - A RGBA color in the form â€œrgba(r,g,b,a)â€
 12743 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12744 â”‚ â”‚                * Where â€œrâ€, â€œgâ€, â€œbâ€ and â€œaâ€ are respectively the red, green, blue and
 12745 â”‚ â”‚                * alpha color values. In the last two cases, â€œrâ€, â€œgâ€, and â€œbâ€ are either integers
 12746 â”‚ â”‚                * in the range 0 to 255 or percentage values in the range 0% to 100%, and
 12747 â”‚ â”‚                * a is a floating point value in the range 0 to 1.
 12748 â”‚ â”‚                * @param spec the string specifying the color
 12749 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the parsing succeeded
 12750 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12751 â”‚ â”‚               parse(spec: string): boolean;
 12752 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12753 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns a textual specification of `rgba` in the form
 12754 â”‚ â”‚                * `rgb(r,g,b)` or
 12755 â”‚ â”‚                * `rgba(r g,b,a)`,
 12756 â”‚ â”‚                * where â€œrâ€, â€œgâ€, â€œbâ€ and â€œaâ€ represent the red, green,
 12757 â”‚ â”‚                * blue and alpha values respectively. â€œrâ€, â€œgâ€, and â€œbâ€ are
 12758 â”‚ â”‚                * represented as integers in the range 0 to 255, and â€œaâ€
 12759 â”‚ â”‚                * is represented as a floating point value in the range 0 to 1.
 12760 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12761 â”‚ â”‚                * These string forms are string forms that are supported by
 12762 â”‚ â”‚                * the CSS3 colors module, and can be parsed by gdk_rgba_parse().
 12763 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12764 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that this string representation may lose some
 12765 â”‚ â”‚                * precision, since â€œrâ€, â€œgâ€ and â€œbâ€ are represented as 8-bit
 12766 â”‚ â”‚                * integers. If this is a concern, you should use a
 12767 â”‚ â”‚                * different representation.
 12768 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns A newly allocated text string
 12769 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12770 â”‚ â”‚               to_string(): string;
 12771 â”‚ â”‚           }
 12772 â”‚ â”‚   
 12773 â”‚ â”‚           /**
 12774 â”‚ â”‚            * Defines the position and size of a rectangle. It is identical to
 12775 â”‚ â”‚            * #cairo_rectangle_int_t.
 12776 â”‚ â”‚            */
 12777 â”‚ â”‚           class Rectangle {
 12778 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<Rectangle>;
 12779 â”‚ â”‚   
 12780 â”‚ â”‚               // Fields
 12781 â”‚ â”‚   
 12782 â”‚ â”‚               x: number;
 12783 â”‚ â”‚               y: number;
 12784 â”‚ â”‚               width: number;
 12785 â”‚ â”‚               height: number;
 12786 â”‚ â”‚   
 12787 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructors
 12788 â”‚ â”‚   
 12789 â”‚ â”‚               constructor(
 12790 â”‚ â”‚                   properties?: Partial<{
 12791 â”‚ â”‚                       x: number;
 12792 â”‚ â”‚                       y: number;
 12793 â”‚ â”‚                       width: number;
 12794 â”‚ â”‚                       height: number;
 12795 â”‚ â”‚                   }>,
 12796 â”‚ â”‚               );
 12797 â”‚ â”‚               _init(...args: any[]): void;
 12798 â”‚ â”‚   
 12799 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
 12800 â”‚ â”‚   
 12801 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12802 â”‚ â”‚                * Checks if the two given rectangles are equal.
 12803 â”‚ â”‚                * @param rect2 a #GdkRectangle
 12804 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the rectangles are equal.
 12805 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12806 â”‚ â”‚               equal(rect2: Rectangle): boolean;
 12807 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12808 â”‚ â”‚                * Calculates the intersection of two rectangles. It is allowed for
 12809 â”‚ â”‚                * `dest` to be the same as either `src1` or `src2`. If the rectangles
 12810 â”‚ â”‚                * do not intersect, `destâ€™`s width and height is set to 0 and its x
 12811 â”‚ â”‚                * and y values are undefined. If you are only interested in whether
 12812 â”‚ â”‚                * the rectangles intersect, but not in the intersecting area itself,
 12813 â”‚ â”‚                * pass %NULL for `dest`.

 12818 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12819 â”‚ â”‚                * Calculates the union of two rectangles.
 12820 â”‚ â”‚                * The union of rectangles `src1` and `src2` is the smallest rectangle which
 12821 â”‚ â”‚                * includes both `src1` and `src2` within it.
 12822 â”‚ â”‚                * It is allowed for `dest` to be the same as either `src1` or `src2`.
 12823 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12824 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that this function does not ignore 'empty' rectangles (ie. with
 12825 â”‚ â”‚                * zero width or height).
 12826 â”‚ â”‚                * @param src2 a #GdkRectangle

 12829 â”‚ â”‚           }

 12889 â”‚ â”‚   
 12890 â”‚ â”‚           /**
 12891 â”‚ â”‚            * A #GdkEvent contains a union of all of the event types,
 12892 â”‚ â”‚            * and allows access to the data fields in a number of ways.
 12893 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12894 â”‚ â”‚            * The event type is always the first field in all of the event types, and
 12895 â”‚ â”‚            * can always be accessed with the following code, no matter what type of
 12896 â”‚ â”‚            * event it is:
 12897 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12898 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
 12899 â”‚ â”‚            *   GdkEvent *event;
 12900 â”‚ â”‚            *   GdkEventType type;
 12901 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12902 â”‚ â”‚            *   type = event->type;
 12903 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
 12904 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12905 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12906 â”‚ â”‚            * To access other fields of the event, the pointer to the event
 12907 â”‚ â”‚            * can be cast to the appropriate event type, or the union member
 12908 â”‚ â”‚            * name can be used. For example if the event type is %GDK_BUTTON_PRESS
 12909 â”‚ â”‚            * then the x coordinate of the button press can be accessed with:
 12910 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12911 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
 12912 â”‚ â”‚            *   GdkEvent *event;
 12913 â”‚ â”‚            *   gdouble x;
 12914 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12915 â”‚ â”‚            *   x = ((GdkEventButton*)event)->x;
 12916 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
 12917 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12918 â”‚ â”‚            * or:
 12919 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12920 â”‚ â”‚            * ```c
 12921 â”‚ â”‚            *   GdkEvent *event;
 12922 â”‚ â”‚            *   gdouble x;
 12923 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12924 â”‚ â”‚            *   x = event->button.x;
 12925 â”‚ â”‚            * ```
 12926 â”‚ â”‚            *
 12927 â”‚ â”‚            */
 12928 â”‚ â”‚           class Event {
 12929 â”‚ â”‚               static $gtype: GObject.GType<Event>;
 12930 â”‚ â”‚   
 12931 â”‚ â”‚               // Fields
 12932 â”‚ â”‚   
 12933 â”‚ â”‚               type: EventType;
 12934 â”‚ â”‚   
 12935 â”‚ â”‚               // Constructors
 12936 â”‚ â”‚   
 12937 â”‚ â”‚               constructor(type: EventType);
 12938 â”‚ â”‚               _init(...args: any[]): void;
 12939 â”‚ â”‚   
 12940 â”‚ â”‚               static ['new'](type: EventType): Event;
 12941 â”‚ â”‚   
 12942 â”‚ â”‚               // Static methods
 12943 â”‚ â”‚   
 12944 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12945 â”‚ â”‚                * Checks all open displays for a #GdkEvent to process,to be processed
 12946 â”‚ â”‚                * on, fetching events from the windowing system if necessary.
 12947 â”‚ â”‚                * See gdk_display_get_event().
 12948 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12949 â”‚ â”‚               static get(): Event | null;
 12950 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12951 â”‚ â”‚                * Sets the function to call to handle all events from GDK.
 12952 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12953 â”‚ â”‚                * Note that GTK+ uses this to install its own event handler, so it is
 12954 â”‚ â”‚                * usually not useful for GTK+ applications. (Although an application
 12955 â”‚ â”‚                * can call this function then call gtk_main_do_event() to pass
 12956 â”‚ â”‚                * events to GTK+.)
 12957 â”‚ â”‚                * @param func the function to call to handle events from GDK.
 12958 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12959 â”‚ â”‚               static handler_set(func: EventFunc): void;
 12960 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12961 â”‚ â”‚                * If there is an event waiting in the event queue of some open
 12962 â”‚ â”‚                * display, returns a copy of it. See gdk_display_peek_event().
 12963 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12964 â”‚ â”‚               static peek(): Event | null;
 12965 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12966 â”‚ â”‚                * Request more motion notifies if `event` is a motion notify hint event.
 12967 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12968 â”‚ â”‚                * This function should be used instead of gdk_window_get_pointer() to
 12969 â”‚ â”‚                * request further motion notifies, because it also works for extension
 12970 â”‚ â”‚                * events where motion notifies are provided for devices other than the
 12971 â”‚ â”‚                * core pointer. Coordinate extraction, processing and requesting more
 12972 â”‚ â”‚                * motion events from a %GDK_MOTION_NOTIFY event usually works like this:
 12973 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12974 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12975 â”‚ â”‚                * ```c
 12976 â”‚ â”‚                * {
 12977 â”‚ â”‚                *   // motion_event handler
 12978 â”‚ â”‚                *   x = motion_event->x;
 12979 â”‚ â”‚                *   y = motion_event->y;
 12980 â”‚ â”‚                *   // handle (x,y) motion
 12981 â”‚ â”‚                *   gdk_event_request_motions (motion_event); // handles is_hint events
 12982 â”‚ â”‚                * }
 12983 â”‚ â”‚                * ```
 12984 â”‚ â”‚                *
 12985 â”‚ â”‚                * @param event a valid #GdkEvent
 12986 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12987 â”‚ â”‚               static request_motions(event: EventMotion): void;
 12988 â”‚ â”‚   
 12989 â”‚ â”‚               // Methods
 12990 â”‚ â”‚   
 12991 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 12992 â”‚ â”‚                * If both events contain X/Y information, this function will return %TRUE
 12993 â”‚ â”‚                * and return in `angle` the relative angle from `event1` to `event2`. The rotation
 12994 â”‚ â”‚                * direction for positive angles is from the positive X axis towards the positive
 12995 â”‚ â”‚                * Y axis.
 12996 â”‚ â”‚                * @param event2 second #GdkEvent
 12997 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the angle could be calculated.
 12998 â”‚ â”‚                */
 12999 â”‚ â”‚               _get_angle(event2: Event): [boolean, number];
 13000 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13001 â”‚ â”‚                * If both events contain X/Y information, the center of both coordinates
 13002 â”‚ â”‚                * will be returned in `x` and `y`.
 13003 â”‚ â”‚                * @param event2 second #GdkEvent
 13004 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the center could be calculated.
 13005 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13006 â”‚ â”‚               _get_center(event2: Event): [boolean, number, number];
 13007 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13008 â”‚ â”‚                * If both events have X/Y information, the distance between both coordinates
 13009 â”‚ â”‚                * (as in a straight line going from `event1` to `event2`) will be returned.

 13011 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the distance could be calculated.
 13012 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13013 â”‚ â”‚               _get_distance(event2: Event): [boolean, number];
 13014 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 13016 â”‚ â”‚                * resources associated with it (e.g. #GdkWindowâ€™s and strings).
 13017 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns a copy of @event. The returned #GdkEvent should be freed with gdk_event_free().
 13018 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13019 â”‚ â”‚               copy(): Event;
 13020 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 13025 â”‚ â”‚                */

 13027 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 13121 â”‚ â”‚                */

 13123 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13124 â”‚ â”‚                * Retrieves the scroll deltas from a #GdkEvent
 13125 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13126 â”‚ â”‚                * See also: gdk_event_get_scroll_direction()
 13127 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the event contains smooth scroll information   and %FALSE otherwise
 13128 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13129 â”‚ â”‚               get_scroll_deltas(): [boolean, number, number];
 13130 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13131 â”‚ â”‚                * Extracts the scroll direction from an event.
 13132 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13133 â”‚ â”‚                * If `event` is not of type %GDK_SCROLL, the contents of `direction`
 13134 â”‚ â”‚                * are undefined.
 13135 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13136 â”‚ â”‚                * If you wish to handle both discrete and smooth scrolling, you
 13137 â”‚ â”‚                * should check the return value of this function, or of
 13138 â”‚ â”‚                * gdk_event_get_scroll_deltas(); for instance:
 13139 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13140 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13141 â”‚ â”‚                * ```c
 13142 â”‚ â”‚                *   GdkScrollDirection direction;
 13143 â”‚ â”‚                *   double vscroll_factor = 0.0;
 13144 â”‚ â”‚                *   double x_scroll, y_scroll;
 13145 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13146 â”‚ â”‚                *   if (gdk_event_get_scroll_direction (event, &direction))
 13147 â”‚ â”‚                *     {
 13148 â”‚ â”‚                *       // Handle discrete scrolling with a known constant delta;
 13149 â”‚ â”‚                *       const double delta = 12.0;
 13150 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13151 â”‚ â”‚                *       switch (direction)
 13152 â”‚ â”‚                *         {
 13153 â”‚ â”‚                *         case GDK_SCROLL_UP:
 13154 â”‚ â”‚                *           vscroll_factor = -delta;
 13155 â”‚ â”‚                *           break;
 13156 â”‚ â”‚                *         case GDK_SCROLL_DOWN:
 13157 â”‚ â”‚                *           vscroll_factor = delta;
 13158 â”‚ â”‚                *           break;
 13159 â”‚ â”‚                *         default:
 13160 â”‚ â”‚                *           // no scrolling
 13161 â”‚ â”‚                *           break;
 13162 â”‚ â”‚                *         }
 13163 â”‚ â”‚                *     }
 13164 â”‚ â”‚                *   else if (gdk_event_get_scroll_deltas (event, &x_scroll, &y_scroll))
 13165 â”‚ â”‚                *     {
 13166 â”‚ â”‚                *       // Handle smooth scrolling directly
 13167 â”‚ â”‚                *       vscroll_factor = y_scroll;
 13168 â”‚ â”‚                *     }
 13169 â”‚ â”‚                * ```
 13170 â”‚ â”‚                *
 13171 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if the event delivered a scroll direction   and %FALSE otherwise
 13172 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13173 â”‚ â”‚               get_scroll_direction(): [boolean, ScrollDirection];
 13174 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13175 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the #GdkSeat this event was generated for.
 13176 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns The #GdkSeat of this event
 13177 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13178 â”‚ â”‚               get_seat(): Seat;
 13179 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13180 â”‚ â”‚                * This function returns the hardware (slave) #GdkDevice that has
 13181 â”‚ â”‚                * triggered the event, falling back to the virtual (master) device
 13182 â”‚ â”‚                * (as in gdk_event_get_device()) if the event wasnâ€™t caused by
 13183 â”‚ â”‚                * interaction with a hardware device. This may happen for example

 13190 â”‚ â”‚                */

 13192 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13193 â”‚ â”‚                * If the event contains a â€œstateâ€ field, puts that field in `state`. Otherwise
 13194 â”‚ â”‚                * stores an empty state (0). Returns %TRUE if there was a state field
 13195 â”‚ â”‚                * in the event. `event` may be %NULL, in which case itâ€™s treated
 13196 â”‚ â”‚                * as if the event had no state field.
 13197 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns %TRUE if there was a state field in the event
 13198 â”‚ â”‚                */
 13199 â”‚ â”‚               get_state(): [boolean, ModifierType];
 13200 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13201 â”‚ â”‚                * Returns the time stamp from `event,` if there is one; otherwise
 13202 â”‚ â”‚                * returns #GDK_CURRENT_TIME. If `event` is %NULL, returns #GDK_CURRENT_TIME.

 13204 â”‚ â”‚                */

 13206 â”‚ â”‚               /**

 13208 â”‚ â”‚                * @returns The #GdkWindow associated with the event
 13209 â”‚ â”‚                */

 13211 â”‚ â”‚               /**
 13212 â”‚ â”‚                * Check whether a scroll event is a stop scroll event. Scroll sequences
 13213 â”‚ â”‚                * with smooth scroll information may provide a stop scroll event once the
 13214 â”‚ â”‚                * interaction with the device finishes, e.g. by lifting a finger. This
 13215 â”‚ â”‚                * stop scroll event is the signal that a widget may trigger kinetic
